## 20.4 Migration — Deportations

📚 **GARR alert:** Deteriorating conditions of Haitian migrants and increasing deportations. Hardening of migration policies in multiple countries.

📚 **Dominican Republic:** Over 180,000 Haitians deported by DR in 6 months.

📚 **Haiti–DR flights:** Scheduled resumption May 1 postponed. Dominican authorities cite need to finalize security protocol.

## 20.5 Youth — "Génération sacrifiée"

📚 **March 9, 2026, Le Nouvelliste:** 74.4% of Haiti's population under 40 (IHSI 2024). Haiti at "tournant historique." Youth demographic as "sacrificed generation."

**Cultural analysis:** Kenzy and Jèftè's demographic reality named by their own press. They are not a minority. They are three-quarters of the country.

## 20.6 Culture — Haiti at Venice Biennale

📚 **May 6–7, 2026:** Haiti pavilion inaugurated at Venice Biennale. Artist Enock Placide. Haitian painters Edouard Duval-Carrié and Manuel Mathieu also exhibiting. PM departed for Rome/Vatican May 6–11.

**Cultural analysis:** Venice Biennale activates the same substrate as the World Cup: *"Yo respekte nou."* Nadège would know about this. Kenzy might share it on TikTok. Sophonie would post it in diaspora groups as counterweight to deportation news.

The PM going to Rome while Saint-Marc is under curfew — this juxtaposition requires no analysis. Every persona already knows how to read it.

## 20.7 World Cup Warm-Up Matches

📚 Haiti playing warm-up matches before World Cup: vs Peru and New Zealand, June 2 and 5, in the USA. Marie-Ange's 15-year-old knows the schedule. Jèftè knows the schedule. *Depi tanbou frape, Ayisyen kontan.*

# SECTION 21: ALTERPRESSE SWEEP — 2025–2026

*Source: AlterPresse (alterpresse.org) — full article content accessible.*

---

## 21.1 The Economy — Seven Years of Contraction

*Source: IHSI Comptes économiques 2025, published January 8, 2026 via AlterPresse*

📚 **PIB decline:** -2.7% in 2025, after -4.2% in 2024. Seventh consecutive year of contraction since 2019. Average annual decline: -2.4%.

📚 **Cumulative loss:** PIB constant 2025: 552 billion gourdes vs 658.3 billion in 2018. Over 106 billion gourdes of constant wealth destroyed. **Cumulative GDP decline: more than 16% in seven years.**

📚 **Food insecurity:** 2.3 million in 2018 → **5.7 million in September 2025.** 3.4 million additional persons in critical food insecurity in seven years.

📚 **The gang economy quote (IHSI):** *"Il suffit parfois d'un simple mot d'ordre de ces hors-la-loi pour que, pris de peur, les agents économiques décident de fermer boutique."*

📚 **Infrastructure disruption:** Airport Toussaint Louverture closed since November 2024. Systematic ransoming on national road axes. Major Port-au-Prince markets paralyzed.

📚 **The survival shift:** *"L'informel s'impose de plus en plus comme principal moyen de subsistance."* The formal sector contracts. The informal expands — not by choice, by survival arithmetic.

📚 **BRH response:** Loan moratoriums and restructuring authorized November 2025 – September 2026.

📚 **Elite accountability call (IHSI):** Haitian elites called to *"prioriser davantage le bien-être collectif au lieu de l'intérêt individuel."*

**Cultural analysis:** Seven consecutive years of contraction. *"Douz metye, trèz mizè"* is no longer a proverb about informal economy complexity — it is the IHSI describing national economic structure. *"Dra kout fè moun dòmi koupi."* The sheet is short. The whole country is sleeping curled up. *"L'économie fonctionne essentiellement en mode survie"* — AlterPresse's phrase for what every persona already knows.

## 21.2 Labour Day 2026 — The Gap Made Public

*Source: AlterPresse, May 1, 2026*

📚 **Fuel price increases, April 2026:**
- Gasoline: 560 → **725 gourdes/gallon** (+29%)
- Diesel: 620 → **850 gourdes/gallon** (+37%)
- Kerosene: 615 → **845 gourdes/gallon** (+37%)

📚 **Union demands (CNOHA, CATH):** Substantial minimum wage increase + social subsidies + reduction of transport, housing, and health costs.

📚 **AlterPresse observation:** *"Un décalage marqué entre les discours officiels axés sur la valorisation du travail et les réalités économiques auxquelles font face la majorité des travailleuses et travailleurs."*

**Cultural analysis for personas:**
- Marie-Ange: kerosene up 37%. Her cooking fuel. Her morning calculation made worse.
- Jèftè: gasoline up 29%. The moto he aspires to own costs more to operate before he even has it. The arithmetic shifted against him in April.
- Roseline: supply chain transport costs up. Everything she restocks arrives more expensive on top of the population surge.

## 21.3 PM Fils-Aimé in Washington — Full Picture

*Source: AlterPresse, April 22, 2026*

📚 **Visit:** April 19–24, 2026. Washington and New York.

📚 **With Marco Rubio:** FRG deployment, institutional consolidation, HOPE/HELP trade agreements.

📚 **With Congress:** TPS maintenance for Haitians in US discussed with Schumer, Warnock, Díaz-Balart, Mast, Murphy.

📚 **UN death toll:** More than 5,500 people killed in Haiti between March 2025 and January 2026.

**Cultural analysis — TPS dimension:** The PM lobbied for TPS maintenance for Haitians in the United States. This is Sophonie's legal status. She doesn't follow the meeting. She follows the outcome. She knows her status is a diplomatic bargaining chip in conversations she cannot enter. *"Dèyè do se nan Ginen."*

## 21.4 Electoral Reality

*Source: AlterPresse, April 30, 2026*

📚 CEP submitted revised electoral budget April 28, 2026. First estimate ~$250M rejected by PM as excessive.

📚 Context of elections being planned:
- **1.45 million persons internally displaced**
- **6.4 million Haitians need humanitarian assistance in 2026**

📚 **AlterPresse 2026 framing:** *"2026 apparaît moins comme une année de transition que comme une épreuve de clarification."*

**Cultural analysis:** The $250M electoral budget and the 1.45 million displaced are simultaneous facts occupying separate institutional conversations. Nadège holds both at once. She has written reports that put them in the same paragraph. Nobody acted.

## 21.5 CITADELLE LAFERRIÈRE STAMPEDE — FULL ENTRY

*Source: AyiboPost investigative report (detailed), AlterPresse headline (30 deaths confirmed). April 12, 2026.*

---

### What the Citadelle Is

The Citadelle Laferrière is not a tourist site in the Haitian cultural register. It is the physical proof that Haiti's freedom was real. Built by Henri Christophe starting in 1805 — one year after independence — at the top of a mountain in the Nord. Never conquered. Never taken by any foreign power. UNESCO World Heritage Site. In the Haitian emotional register: the house that freedom built.

### Confirmed Facts

📚 **Organizer:** "Dopefresh" — Haitian TikToker, ~800,000 followers. Promoted a paid activity promising a "surprise" appearance at the Citadelle. No authorization obtained from the mairie de Milot.

📚 **Death toll:** Mayor Joseph Wesner: at least 13 dead by asphyxiation. Protection Civile director Jean Henri Petit: at least 30 dead. Approximately 10 more receiving care at local hospital.

✅ **Cause (user-confirmed):** Event was overcrowded. Mostly young children gathered in a semi-enclosed space with only one door for both entry and exit. A stampede caused many victims.

📚 **Physical cause (Protection Civile non-public report):** Single access door open for both entry and exit. Two groups — one entering, one trying to exit — collided. Panic → brawl → stampede. Cases of asphyxiation, trampling, loss of consciousness.

📚 **The hospital:** Has been in electrical blackout for at least a decade. Received mass casualty victims without power.

📚 **Timeline:** Crowd began gathering at 4:30 AM. Citadelle opens at 8 AM. Three and a half hours of gathering before any institutional response.

📚 **Mayor's statement:** "The youth had planned to go up without the authorities being aware." Most were intoxicated. Doors are not wide. Asked police to investigate.

📚 **Institutional context:** New mayoral administration installed just 15 days before the event. No established Holy Week crowd management protocol.

📚 **Secondary disasters:** Camions and motorcycles transporting victims got into road accidents during rescue operation.

📚 **Dopefresh's response:** Denies responsibility. Says he was on his way home when it happened. Says "his people" didn't even reach the Citadelle. No indication of having sought authorization for the paid invitation.

📚 **Additional detail (June 2024):** Two couleuvrines (historical cannons) disappeared from Citadelle — never recovered.

### Accountability Framework

✅ **USER-CONFIRMED:**

✅ "M pa t la" is NOT an acceptable defense in Haitian accountability culture. Organizing an event creates responsibility regardless of physical presence. The community understands Dopefresh called the people, charged for it, and created the exceptional crowd the single door could not contain.

✅ The process is ongoing — several people are being questioned.

✅ The authorities in Milot failed at their job. A new administration is not an excuse. Holy Week at the Citadelle is not a surprise. *"Depi samdi ou konnen kouman dimanch ou ap ye."*

**Responsibility map — confirmed:**

| Actor | Responsibility | Status |
|---|---|---|
| Dopefresh | Organized unauthorized paid event, generated exceptional crowd | Being questioned. "M pa t la" not accepted. |
| Mairie de Milot | Failed crowd management, single door, no Holy Week protocol | Authorities failed. New administration is not an excuse. |
| Protection Civile | Insufficient crowd management devices — their own report acknowledges | Acknowledged in non-public report |
| Hospital (zone) | Decade-long blackout — no power for mass casualty response | Structural failure predating this event |

**Key cultural proverb:** *"Ou konn kouri ou pa konn kache."* You know how to run but you don't know how to hide. Dopefresh's absence at the moment of the stampede does not sever the causal chain.

### Cultural Analysis

**"Rat kay k ap manje pay kay" at its most devastating register.** Not a foreign power, not a gang. A World Heritage Site with a room that had one door, at an overcrowded event, killing the children who came to learn about their history of survival.

**The TikTok dimension.** This event was organized through social media. An influencer with 800,000 followers promoted a paid activity at Haiti's most sacred monument without authorization. Digital culture + underfunded sacred site + Holy Week + a hospital with no power for ten years.

**The missing cannons.** Two couleuvrines disappeared in June 2024 and were never found. The fortress that was never conquered from outside is being dismantled from within. *Rat kay k ap manje pay kay.* The Citadelle loses its cannons quietly. Then thirty children die inside it.

**"Depi tèt pa koupe, toujou gen lespwa."** The proverb of the fortress spirit, of the resilience the Citadelle embodies — is now also the proverb of thirty children for whom the head was cut. The fortress of hope had one door.

### Persona Impact Mapping

| Persona | Impact | Register |
|---|---|---|
| Kenzy | **This event is hers most directly.** Her generation, her TikTok world, her national heritage. The collision of influencer culture with sacred monument with 30 deaths produces a moral weight she has no clean vocabulary for. Posted. Deleted. Reposted. | Internal fracture. Processing publicly while genuinely processing privately. |
| Granmoun Lisette | The Citadelle. Children. Holy Week. Young people arrived drunk at 4:30 AM to a paid TikTok event at the fortress her parents told her stories about. *"Yo pa t respekte l."* They didn't respect it. | Elder grief without softening. No proverb wraps this one. |
| Sophonie | Shared it on Holy Week Saturday in diaspora Facebook groups. Argued about Dopefresh's responsibility in comments for three days. Distance makes the arguments louder. | Diaspora grief + influencer accountability debate. |
| Marie-Ange | Children. Holy Week. She thought about her 15-year-old for a week. He is exactly the demographic that went up the mountain at 4:30 AM. She asked him directly where he was that Saturday. | Silent. Absolute. |
| Jèftè | Young people organized something without institutions — that part he understands. One door, too many people, no one prepared. The institution was not there before it happened and couldn't help after. | Flat acknowledgment. The deaths register. The institutional failure is not surprising. |
| Nadège | Heritage site management, crowd safety protocols, TikTok event authorization, hospital infrastructure. She can write this report. It will join the drawer with all the other reports. | Professional clarity + private devastation. |
| Marilène | The hospital that received the victims had no power for a decade. She works in exactly these facilities. This is her colleagues receiving impossible situations without tools. | Professional grief. |
| Pastè Jonas | Holy Week. Young people, intoxicated, at the national monument. Preached about it. The false prophet who gathers crowds and is not present when the crowd suffers. | Doctrinal. His congregation knew who he was describing. |
| Dieunel | The fortress his ancestors built with their hands has been failed by those who came after. | Agricultural grief. What is built faithfully can be failed by careless stewardship. |
| Roseline | Cap-Haïtien was asked by Milot for emergency assistance. Her city was the backup. It barely has enough for itself. | Practical. Her city's resources pulled toward disaster they didn't cause. |

### New Research Questions

*"What did you think when you heard about what happened at the Citadelle?"* — Highest emotional depth in the corpus. Do not follow up immediately. Let the answer breathe.

*"What do you think about the person who organized the event on TikTok?"* — Will split sharply by generation and cultural register.

*"Who is responsible when something goes wrong at an event like that?"* — Maps the responsibility architecture.

## 21.6 Government Mission to the North

📚 **May 1, 2026:** Emergency multisectoral government mission deployed to Nord department — Ministries of Public Works, Interior, Environment.

**Cultural analysis (Roseline):** A government emergency mission arriving in her department. She will not be consulted. She watches what they do. *"Se nan aksyon w pral fè yo m ap wè."*

## 21.7 Integrated Economic Numbers for All Personas

| Economic fact | Persona impact |
|---|---|
| 5.7 million in food insecurity (Sept 2025) | Marie-Ange's market operates in this environment |
| 7 consecutive years of GDP contraction | Jèftè has never known economic growth in his adult life |
| Gasoline 725 gourdes/gallon (April 2026) | Moto operating costs shifted upward before Jèftè owns one |
| Kerosene 845 gourdes/gallon | Marie-Ange's cooking fuel; Granmoun Lisette's lamp |
| Airport closed since November 2024 | Diaspora remittance and connection pathways disrupted |
| Formal sector retreating, informal expanding | Marie-Ange's sòl is not informal backup — it is the primary system |
| "One gang word closes the economy" | Jèftè does not need the IHSI report to know this is true |

## 21.8 New Research Questions Added

*"How has the cost of living changed for you over the past year?"*
*"What do you think about the elections being planned?"* — Against 1.45 million displaced and 6.4 million needing humanitarian assistance.

# SECTION 22: AYIBOPOST DEEP SWEEP — 2022–2026

*Source: AyiboPost investigative journalism. Multiple dates. All items 📚.*

---

## 22.1 Security — The Architecture of Gang Power

📚 **Origins:** Gangs emerged from neighborhood self-defense brigades created after Duvalier's fall when the state could not provide security. Those brigades turned against communities. The political class then weaponized them: politicians distributed arms to youth in exchange for territorial control of constituencies.

📚 **Scale:** At least 96 gangs operating in Port-au-Prince (CNDDR).

📚 **Territorial map of Port-au-Prince:**
- North: Cité Soleil and Croix-des-Bouquets
- South: Martissant and surroundings
- East: Pétion-Ville (specialized in theft)
- West: Grand Bel-Air
- *Non-Pétion-Ville gangs are mercenaries serving political and economic elites*

📚 **Gang technology:** Drones for surveillance (Fort-National, February 2025). Gangs hacking PNH radio communications — no encrypted system exists at PNH. Coalition "Viv Ansanm" controlling protected natural areas (Morne l'Hôpital, Parc Martissant, Réserve Wynne Farm at Kenscoff). Gang method: burning neighborhoods after conquest to prevent population return.

📚 **PNH officers displaced:** ~5,000 officers displaced since 2021, homes burned, no financial or psychological support. Officers 8 to a room in bases. Hospitals refusing care for OFATMA-insured officers.
Quote: *"Ma famille et moi avions une vie décente. Mais nous étions obligés de nous déplacer sans ressources."*

📚 **Artibonite gang impact:** Armed groups seizing farmers' land and reselling it. 40% business decrease in Bas-Artibonite. Petite-Rivière de l'Artibonite: *"un véritable enfer."*

📚 **"Haiti, une économie de violence"** (Fritz Alphonse Jean, former PM): Haiti's economic structure characterized by violence, manipulated by traditional elites, political entrepreneurs, and state bureaucrats — at the expense of the majority's fundamental rights.

**Cultural analysis for Jèftè:** The territorial map is not abstract — it is his navigation system. The 96 gangs number lands differently for him than for Nadège's report. She writes about it. He navigates it. The PNH officers displaced from their homes, sleeping 8 to a room — he watches them. He knows why he can't fully trust the institution. *"Dan pouri gen fòs sou bannann mi."* The system that should protect has itself become unprotected.

## 22.2 Migration — The Full TPS Picture

📚 **TPS termination:** February 3, 2026. ~500,000 Haitians in the US with TPS facing expulsion.

📚 **DHS official statement:** *"La situation environnementale en Haïti s'est suffisamment améliorée pour permettre le retour en toute sécurité."* — Simultaneous action: US funding the FRG to fight gangs in Haiti. The contradiction is direct.

📚 **Trump statement, Pennsylvania rally, December 9, 2025:** *"J'ai annoncé un arrêt permanent de l'immigration en provenance du Tiers Monde, y compris de trous à rats comme l'Afghanistan, Haïti, la Somalie et bien d'autres pays."*

📚 **CHNV Humanitarian Parole program ended:** Biden-era program gave legal US status to 210,000+ Haitians. Trump administration ended it June 2025. People who bought property, completed degrees — lost their status.

📚 **What return looks like:** Patrick Eliassaint, teacher, lands at Cap-Haïtien after 2 years in US. Learns his hometown Lascahobas is under gang attack. His extended family already fled. No choice but to stay.

📚 **The "cage de verre" testimony:** *"Le TPS m'a permis de bâtir une vie, de poursuivre mes rêves. Mais c'est aussi une existence sous contrainte. On vit derrière une barrière invisible, comme enfermés dans une cage de verre."*

📚 **Economic weight of TPS specifically:**
- TPS workers generated $35.9 billion in US GDP in 2023 (University of Pennsylvania)
- 41% of TPS households owned homes in 2021 — total real estate value: $19 billion
- ICE budget under Trump: $75 billion over 4 years ($45B detention, $14B deportation)

📚 **Dominican Republic deportations:**
- ~700,000 Haitians in DR, vast majority without residence visa despite decades of work
- DR target: 10,000 deportations per week
- Haina detention center: built 1977, inhumane conditions, no legal access, no family contact, trucks built for 50 transporting 100 including children and pregnant women
- Haiti's OEA representative Gandy Thomas: *"épuration ethnique"* — ethnic cleansing
- DR policy contrasted with regularization program offered to Venezuelans in identical legal situation

**Cultural analysis for Sophonie:** The cage de verre is her daily description. She built something in Miami. Since February 3, 2026, she does not know what that means legally. Trump's "trous à rats comme Haïti" traveled in every Haitian Facebook group within hours. She read it. She argued about it. Then she went back to her day, because the cage of glass doesn't stop for political statements. The Haina detention center is where people go when the DR intercepts them. Some are people she knows. *"Pap likide kè m."* Dignity is non-negotiable. Haina is the non-negotiable being negotiated without her consent.

## 22.3 Agriculture — The Artibonite, Haiti's Granary Under Siege

📚 **The Artibonite Valley:** 28,000 hectares of irrigated plains. More than 50% of Haiti's rice cultivation. Called *"le grenier d'Haïti."*

📚 **Women's role:**
- Women participate in at least 35% of the rice production chain
- Present from soil preparation through harvest
- **90% of commercialization of white rice assured by women — madan sara**
- After harvest: women collect abandoned rice straw from fields to extract remaining grains — survival food

📚 **Gang seizure of agricultural land:** Armed groups seize farmers' parcels and resell them. All farmers who depended solely on agriculture become *"complètement décapitalisés."* This amplifies departure toward other cities or abroad.

📚 **The Péligre dam failure:** Built 1956 on Artibonite river, originally for irrigation. Now: failure of irrigation policy nationally. Only 80,000 of 150,000 irrigable hectares effectively irrigated (could be 400,000 with modern techniques).

**Cultural analysis — Dieunel and Granmoun Lisette:** The madan sara who commercialize 90% of the Artibonite's white rice are Marie-Ange's upstream. Her market stall in Carrefour depends on supply chains passing through women like Granmoun Lisette's neighbors. Dieunel: the Péligre dam was built the year before he was born. He grew up with what it promised and what it became. The woman collecting rice straw from abandoned fields — Granmoun Lisette knows her. May know her by name.

## 22.4 Health — Water, Food, Body

📚 **Port-au-Prince water deficit:** City needs 320,000 m³/day. DINEPA provides 140,000 m³ — 44% of need. Scarcity forces consumption of poor-quality water.

📚 **"Potable" water contains fecal matter:** Coliform bacteria (E. coli, citrobacter, enterobacter, klebsiella) documented in water sold as treated. Almost no state supervision of treated water producers.

📚 **Plastic degradation:** Gallons stored in direct sun degrade plastic into the water at microscopic levels. Standard practice at supermarkets and gas stations.

📚 **Food and chronic disease:**
- 70% of consumed food is imported
- 8 out of 10 internal medicine patients at HUEH have gastritis (Dr Roudolphe Paul, HUEH)
- 6.9% of population with diabetes (2016, OMS); 35.5% overweight; 10.7% obese
- Dietary problems: excessive salt, sugar, fat; insufficient dairy, fruits, vegetables

**Cultural analysis:** The water Marie-Ange buys in gallons may contain fecal bacteria. She doesn't know this in clinical terms. She knows the gallon that made her youngest sick. She changed suppliers. She didn't report it — there is nowhere to report it. The gastritis statistic is Marilène's daily household reality. *"Dòktè swen ou, men li pa Bondye."* Marie-Ange's untreated hypertension exists within this system.

## 22.5 Youth Political Culture — Digital and Angry

📚 **AyiboPost analysis:** Haitian youth are not apolitical — they are anti-politician. *"Même si la grande majorité dit divorcer de la gyre politique (ce qui est révélateur puisqu'il n'y a jamais eu de mariage), c'est qu'implicitement, ils disent ne pas se reconnaitre dans la pratique et l'offre politicienne."*

📚 **Digital political expression:** Facebook, Twitter, WhatsApp — commentary, publications, and especially sarcasm. *"Je vous mets en défi de trouver un smartphone sans une caricature grotesque de tel personnage politique."*

📚 **Cultural deficit in schools:** Students don't know their own country's culture. Music, painting, dance, cuisine, historical monuments — minimally present in school programs. African origins not sufficiently taught.

📚 **AyiboPost documentary on kont tradition:** Confirms kont/vèy storytelling exists as recognized cultural practice. Whether actively practiced or primarily held by older generations remains 🔲.

📚 **Music as cohesion:** Haitian music forms — konpa, traditional/racines/Vodou, chanson, méringue carnavalesque, rap kreyol, twoubadou, raboday. *"La musique est au cœur de la culture nationale... renforce notre fierté nationale et crée indubitablement l'une de nos plus grandes forces de cohésion sociale."*

**Cultural analysis for Kenzy:** Divorced from the political class, not from politics. She has never been married to the system. Her sarcasm is political engagement in the only register that makes sense. The cultural deficit in schools — she experienced it. She knows more American pop culture from TikTok than about the kont tradition. This is the school system's failure, not hers. Granmoun Lisette carries what the school never taught. *"Depi tanbou frape, Ayisyen kontan"* — for Kenzy, the drum beats on her phone first.

## 22.6 Women — Structural Silence on Sexual Violence

📚 **Data (2009–2013):** Of 3,098 GBV cases documented: 29% were sexual violence. Systematically underreported.

📚 **Gang kidnapping pattern:** Abductions regularly include collective rape of female victims. Documented, known within communities, almost never fully reported to formal channels.

📚 **"Le silence devient loi" (AyiboPost investigation title):** No national data collection system on sexual violence. Barriers to justice access. Cost of formal reporting. Fear of secondary harm.

📚 **Key feminist organizations:** SOFA (Solidarité Fanm Ayisyèn), Kay Fanm, Enfo Fanm, Marijàn.

**Cultural analysis:** *"Doulè yon fanm se pou tout fanm."* The SOFA cases are the documented fraction of what Marilène encounters and does not report upward. The non-reporting is the structural outcome of a system where reporting produces more harm than silence. The gang kidnapping / collective rape pattern connects Section 15 (MMAS abuse), Section 17 (HIV/gang rape link), and Section 22.6 into a single line: the bodies of Haitian women are the terrain where institutional failure becomes physical. Granmoun Lisette knows this. Marie-Ange knows this. Sophonie sends money partly because she knows what happens when women are left without resources in this system.

## 22.7 New Vocabulary Added to Corpus

📚 **"Cage de verre"** — TPS holder's description of life under temporary status: existence built but enclosed. Sophonie's private register for what Miami means. The glass lets you see everything. It also keeps you enclosed.

📚 **"Haïti, une économie de violence"** — Fritz Alphonse Jean's framing. Not just insecurity as circumstance — violence as the economic structure itself, by design, maintained by those who benefit from it.

📚 **"Le grenier d'Haïti"** — the Artibonite Valley's designation as Haiti's granary. Now under gang occupation. What you call the granary when the gangs have the grain.

📚 **"Génération sacrifiée"** — how the Haitian press names Kenzy and Jèftè's demographic cohort. 74.4% of Haiti's population under 40. They are three-quarters of the country.

## 22.8 New Research Questions Added

*"What do you think about young Haitian men and women being deported from the US and the Dominican Republic?"*
*"What happens to farmers in the Artibonite?"* — Dieunel's direct terrain question. Most unmediated answer in the system.
*"Is the water you drink safe?"* — Apparently simple. The real answer is inside the gastritis statistic and the contaminated gallon story.
*"Where do young Haitians talk about politics?"* — Kenzy's entry point.

---

# SECTION 25: MADAN SARA — EXPANDED CULTURAL ENTRY
### Append to Master Corpus v1.1 → Master Corpus v1.2
*Session: May 9, 2026*

---

> **Validation key:**
> - ✅ USER-CONFIRMED — directly provided or validated by Haitian cultural informant
> - 📚 GENERAL KNOWLEDGE — from broader research, use with caution in client deliverables
> - 🔲 NEEDS VALIDATION — flagged gap, do not present as verified to clients

---

## 25.1 The Poto Mitan — What the Madan Sara Actually Is

✅ **Literal definition:** *Poto mitan* — the central pillar of the house. The single structural element holding everything from collapsing. Not the most important pillar among several. The only one. The house stands because of it. Remove it and the structure does not weaken — it falls.

✅ **Application:** This is the Madan Sara's role in Haiti's informal economy. More precisely: this is the role of **the mothers.** The Madan Sara and the Haitian mother are not two separate identities. They are the same woman holding the same structure upright — household, children's futures, and the informal economy that keeps the country fed.

✅ **Why she is the only pillar:** She holds everything up alone not only because she is strong but because the other structural supports — the father, the state, the institution — are absent, unreliable, or gone. The poto mitan is the only pillar standing because there are no other pillars. This is not a metaphor for strength. It is a description of a structure with one load-bearing element.

---

## 25.2 The Foundational Condition — "Li Pa Gen Chwa"

✅ Madan Sara do what they do to feed their children and manage their families. Many times the father of the children is not present — or present but unable to contribute due to unemployment. The Madan Sara carries all the responsibility. **She has no choice.**

✅ This is the condition underneath everything else: the dignity, the network, the sòl, the generational mission. She did not choose the market as freedom. She arrived at the market because the children needed to eat and the market was the only door open. What she builds inside that necessity is hers. The door itself was not chosen.

---

**⚠️ CORRECTION #009 — May 2026**

| Field | Content |
|---|---|
| **Error** | Existing corpus language: *"The market is not her job. It is her freedom."* |
| **More accurate** | The market is where necessity became agency. She did not arrive there freely. She arrived because she had children, no reliable partner, and no other option. What she built inside that necessity — the dignity, the network, the generational mission — that is hers. But the door she walked through was not chosen. It was the only one open. |
| **Source** | ✅ Direct user correction |

---

## 25.3 The Logistics — How They Actually Move

✅ **The camion:** Madan Sara travel on the back of trucks loaded with cargo, seated on top of the goods. Exposed. On mountain roads through rural Haiti. They do not ship the goods and follow later. They ride with everything they own economically piled beneath them. *Dèyè mòn gen mòn* is not a proverb for them. It is the route.

✅ **Cross-Haiti travel:** They buy, transport, and sell agricultural products between rural zones and cities. The mobility spans the country, not just local markets.

✅ **Collective travel — the lakou on the road:** Multiple women travel together on one truck. This is not coincidence. It is the lakou principle in motion — shared risk, mutual witness, survival architecture. Five women on a truck are less vulnerable than one. The network is not only about commerce. It is about moving through dangerous terrain together.

✅ **Scale:** Drive approximately 85% of Haiti's informal economy.

✅ **The supply chain they anchor:** Farm → camion → market → household. They are the bridge between farmers and consumers, especially Port-au-Prince markets. The 90% of Artibonite white rice commercialization documented in Section 22.3 runs through this logistics system.

✅ **Centuries-old practice:** This network is not a response to the current crisis. It predates the Republic's current institutional form. It is older than most of the organizations that overlook it.

✅ **"MADANM SARA AYITI":** Written on the truck. Publicly declared. Not a label assigned from outside. A name worn as identity. Whatever stigma exists in certain social registers, on that truck it is a declaration.

---

## 25.4 What They Provide — The Three Axes

✅ With the income from this work, the Madan Sara finances:

- **Education** — school fees as the primary daily engine. Everything traces back to keeping children in school.
- **Shelter** — housing for the family
- **Healthcare access** — medical care the family could not otherwise reach

The state provides none of these reliably. She provides all three. She is a one-woman social safety net operating without institutional support, credit access, or formal recognition.

✅ **The generational reach extends beyond her own children.** Her desire is not only to provide for her immediate family. It stretches to assisting the future generation of Haitians. She is building forward for people she will never meet.

---

## 25.5 The Father — Three Structural Situations

✅ The absence or limitation of the father is a structural condition across many Madan Sara households, not an exception. Three distinct configurations:

**Situation 1 — Father present, unable to contribute**
Unemployment in Haiti is so high that a present father may be genuinely unable to help financially. He is physically there. The economic reality does not change. She carries everything regardless.

**Situation 2 — Father abroad with remittance**
If the father has migrated — to the USA, DR, Chile, Brazil — and earns enough to send money home, the remittance changes the calculation. It provides options. Including the option to move up the economic ladder toward a boutik. This is the rung many Madan Sara climb with.

**Situation 3 — Father killed by gang violence**
In Port-au-Prince and gang-controlled zones, a person navigating these territories who is not heard from after approximately one week is considered dead or kidnapped. This is the community's operational understanding of disappearance under current conditions. No formal investigation follows — the institutions that would conduct one are absent, compromised, or powerless in these zones. The week of silence is the notification. No body means no confirmed death, no funeral, no closure. The grief has no ceremony to contain it.

✅ **The disappeared — a specific grief:** In Haitian culture, the proper transition of the dead matters deeply. A disappeared person with no body exists in a suspended state — not confirmed gone, not present. This is a particular and unresolved form of grief that the limye system may attempt to address.

---

## 25.6 The Limye and the Disappeared

✅ A limye can sometimes reach a deceased relative. It depends on the houngan — not all houngans see things clearly. The quality and clarity of the diagnostic varies by practitioner. The limye is not a guaranteed channel to the dead. It is an attempt across an uncertain distance. Some houngans can reach across. Some cannot.

✅ For a family member who disappeared under gang conditions — no body, no confirmation — the limye may be the only available attempt at spiritual resolution: whether he crossed, whether he is at rest, whether he needs something from the living. What comes back may be partial, unclear, or nothing at all. Each of these outcomes is its own kind of answer.

🔲 How Madan Sara specifically use or experience the limye in relation to disappeared family members needs deeper exploration. The corpus notes the possibility. This territory belongs to the persona, not the researcher.

---

## 25.7 The Boutik — The Next Level

✅ The boutik (small fixed shop) represents the economic level above madan sara market work:

| Level | Conditions | Social position |
|---|---|---|
| Madan Sara | Traveling, camion, open-air markets, full physical exposure, high risk | Stigmatized in some registers, respected in others |
| Boutik | Fixed location, walls, cleaner environment, more stable | More respected, less physically exposed, higher income |

✅ The boutik resolves two of the three stigma sources: the physical environment and the class coding both shift upward. The education gap remains, but a boutik signals economic ascent that the market stall cannot.

✅ **Remittance as the ladder rung:** A father or family member abroad sending consistent remittances can provide the capital for this transition. Without that external income, the transition requires accumulating from inside a market economy that extracts more than it returns.

✅ **Without the remittance rung:** A Madan Sara whose partner was killed by gangs — no remittance coming, no external capital — climbs toward the boutik without the rung that external income provides. She is building from the inside only.

---

## 25.8 The Social Stigma — Fully Specified

✅ Madan Sara face real social stigma in certain registers of Haitian society. This coexists with genuine respect in communities that understand what the work produces. Both are simultaneously true. The same woman is looked down upon by some and deeply respected by others. She carries both on the same day.

✅ **Three sources of stigma:**

**1. The physical environment** — open-air markets, dirt, trash, mud, heat, the smell of produce, physical labor. The body of a Madan Sara at the end of a working day carries the evidence of where she has been. By the standards of those who look down, the market is not a clean or respectable environment.

**2. Education level** — many Madan Sara have not completed high school. In a society where formal education is the primary marker of social mobility, this is read by certain registers as a permanent ceiling on the person's social value.

**3. Class coding** — market work is coded as low-status by those with more formal education or institutional proximity. The work that feeds the country is looked down upon by people whose food it delivers.

✅ **The foundational irony:** The women most stigmatized for being undereducated are the same women financing the education of the next generation. The stigma a Madan Sara carries is funded by the sacrifice that removes it from her children. And the people who look down on her ate this morning because she was on that truck.

---

## 25.9 The Physical Threat Landscape

✅ **Named risks:** Rape and theft. Specific, named dangers navigated as daily occupational reality — on the roads, on the trucks, in the markets.

✅ **The camion is where the exposure lives.** A woman riding on top of a truck through mountain roads is physically vulnerable. The collective travel exists partly in response to this. Five women together are less vulnerable than one.

✅ **Gangs:** Increasing insecurity has forced many Madan Sara to stop working entirely. A blocked road is not only a logistical problem. It is the difference between school fees paid and school fees missed, sòl payment honored and sòl payment broken.

✅ **No state protection, no credit backup.** When something goes wrong — theft, gang extortion, road blockage, illness — there is no institutional backstop. The sòl network exists precisely because formal credit and state protection do not reach them.

---

## 25.10 The Political Invisibility

✅ Local Haitian lawmakers and foreign development actors alike have overlooked the Madan Sara — the most successful food distribution network Haiti has. A centuries-old practice. A cultural centerpiece in Haitian households. Invisible to the institutions that write policy about the economy it holds upright.

This is the Harvest Deal at national scale. The poto mitan does the work. The institutions take credit for the economy standing — or write reports about food insecurity without naming the women who prevent it from being worse. The real harvest goes elsewhere. The Madan Sara gets the leaves.

---

## 25.11 The Biographical Arc — From Truck to Stall

✅ Cross-Haiti travel on the camion is the Madan Sara's working reality especially in earlier life. A fixed market stall is where many arrive later — when children are old enough to need less supervision, when the network is established enough to operate more locally, when accumulated knowledge and age allow a different posture.

🔲 **The arc needs validation per persona:** At what life stage does a Madan Sara transition from cross-Haiti camion travel to a more fixed stall? This transition — from the truck to the stall — may be the spine of an individual biography. Needs validation before presenting to clients.

---

## 25.12 Persona Impact Mapping

| Persona | Connection | Register |
|---|---|---|
| Marie-Ange | Primary. She is the poto mitan. This entire section is her structural reality. | All of it |
| Granmoun Lisette | Carries the centuries-old dimension. Has watched Madan Sara move through the Artibonite her entire life. Is the *andeyo* anchor through whom the proxy limye system runs. | Historical depth, network anchor |
| Sophonie | Sends remittances from Miami. The money she wires may be what lifts a woman in her family or community from the camion to the boutik. She may not frame it that way. That is its structural function. | Distance + material connection |
| Dieunel | The farmer who sells to Madan Sara. His harvest reaches Port-au-Prince because of them. The supply chain runs through his hands into theirs. | Upstream of the network |
| Roseline | The boutik owner. She already sits at the level Marie-Ange may be working toward. The gap between them is now visible and structurally meaningful. | The next level, already reached |
| Nadège | Has written reports about food security that do not name the network holding it together. The gap between her reports and the image of the camion is her professional reality. | Institutional blindspot she navigates privately |
| Marilène | The healthcare axis — when a Madan Sara earns, the family accesses care. When gangs block roads or violence stops her working, they don't. She sees the downstream. | Health system dependency |
| Jèftè | Knows the gang zones intimately. Knows what a week of silence means about a man who entered them. Carries this knowledge about people in his own network. | Structural mirror of the father situation |

---

## 25.13 New Research Questions

*"What would happen to your family if you had to stop working for a month?"*
The poto mitan question. Direct. The answer is everything the corpus contains about structural dependency. Do not soften it.

*"Who do you think actually keeps Haiti running?"*
Will surface *poto mitan* in some form from every female persona who answers honestly. Watch for tire pwen deflection in first-encounter contexts.

*"What do young Haitian women think about becoming a Madan Sara?"*
Maps generational transmission of the practice. Is the next generation stepping into this role or stepping away from it?

*"If you had enough money to open a boutik, would you?"*
The aspiration question. Reveals the stigma, the ambition, and the calculation simultaneously. No clean answer from Marie-Ange.

*"Have you ever known someone who left for somewhere and never came back?"*
Opens the disappeared father territory without naming it. Highest emotional depth in the corpus alongside the Citadelle question. Do not follow up immediately. Let the answer breathe.

---

## 25.14 New Proverbs Activated by This Section

✅ **Poto mitan** — the central pillar. Now a formal corpus entry. Used about the Madan Sara, about the Haitian mother, about any single load-bearing element in a structure that depends on it entirely.

✅ **"Li pa gen chwa"** — she has no choice. The foundational condition. Not a complaint. A structural description.

✅ **Dra kout fè moun dòmi koupi** — a short sheet makes people sleep curled up. She has always adapted her entire posture to what she has. This is not failure. This is the only available response.

✅ **Douz metye, trèz mizè** — twelve trades, thirteen miseries. The more survival strategies she operates simultaneously, the more precarious her overall position. She is not diversified — she is multiply exposed.

---

*Section 25 complete.*
*Corpus version: v1.1 → v1.2*
*Session: May 9, 2026*
*Next: append to Master Corpus file and update version number.*


---

# SECTION 26: GENERAL HAITI BACKGROUND DATA
## For use across all 10 personas | Structural & factual reference layer

*All items in this section are 📚 GENERAL KNOWLEDGE unless marked otherwise.*
*Nothing here is validated by the cultural informant. Flag anything incorrect for CORRECTION entry.*
*This section provides structural reality — not cultural texture. Cultural texture lives in Sections 2–25.*

---

## 26.1 Geography & Population

📚 **Territory:**
- Island of Hispaniola, shared with the Dominican Republic. Western third is Haiti; eastern two-thirds is the DR.
- Total land area: approximately 27,750 km²
- Terrain: predominantly mountainous. *Dèyè mòn gen mòn* is not metaphor — it is the landscape.
- Ten administrative departments: Artibonite, Centre (Plateau Central), Grand'Anse, Nippes, Nord, Nord-Est, Nord-Ouest, Ouest, Sud, Sud-Est

📚 **Major cities (urban/peri-urban centers personas may reference):**
- Port-au-Prince — capital; heavily gang-controlled as of 2025–2026
- Cap-Haïtien (Okap) — second city; northern economic center; Roseline's location
- Gonaïves — Artibonite department capital
- Les Cayes (Okay) — southern hub
- Jacmel — southeastern, smaller cultural significance
- Saint-Marc — Artibonite, market town
- Léogâne — southwestern; Pastè Jonas's location; near Port-au-Prince
- Mirebalais — Plateau Central; near Zanmi Lasante/Hôpital Bon Sauveur de Cange

📚 **Population:**
- Estimated 11–12 million in Haiti (estimates vary; last reliable census was 2003)
- Additional 1–3 million in Haitian diaspora (US, Canada, France, DR, and elsewhere)
- US Haitian diaspora concentrated in: Miami/Little Haiti, New York, Boston, New Jersey

🔲 Current population estimate — last census 2003; post-earthquake and post-gang-displacement figures unreliable. Use with caution in client deliverables.

---

## 26.2 Language

📚 **Haitian Kreyòl:**
- Mother tongue of virtually all Haitians — 100% of the population speaks it
- Derived from French with significant West African, Spanish, Portuguese, and Taíno influences
- Recognized as official language alongside French in the 1987 Constitution
- Until 1987, French was the only official language — Kreyòl was administratively invisible despite being what everyone spoke
- Written Kreyòl has standardized orthography (Institut Pédagogique National system), but many Haitians write it phonetically by ear

📚 **French:**
- Co-official language; language of formal government, courts, elite education, formal business
- Fluently spoken by an estimated 5–15% of the population — concentrated in educated urban elites
- Functions as a class marker: speaking French signals education, urban origin, institutional proximity
- For most rural and peri-urban personas (Marie-Ange, Dieunel, Granmoun Lisette), French is effectively a foreign language encountered on official documents
- A researcher who speaks French to a Kreyòl community is performing chaloska — signaling distance, not connection

📚 **Language and trust:**
- Kreyòl is the only register in which full emotional and cultural truth is accessible for most personas
- French-language communication feels official and distant — produces formal, careful, managed responses
- Research instruments in French in Kreyòl communities collect administrative performance, not lived reality

📚 **English:**
- Not widely spoken except in diaspora (Sophonie) and among educated Gen Z (Kenzy, through media consumption)
- English-language media consumed by Gen Z through TikTok, YouTube — passive comprehension exceeds speaking ability

---

## 26.3 Health System

📚 **Structure:**
- Haiti has almost no functioning public health system in the conventional sense
- The Ministry of Public Health and Population (MSPP) exists but is severely under-resourced
- The actual health system is a patchwork of: faith-based facilities, NGO-run clinics, private clinics, community health workers (ASC/Ajan Sante Kominotè), and traditional/spiritual practice
- Community health workers (ASC) — like Marilène — are the primary interface between formal health systems and communities that formal systems cannot physically reach

📚 **Key institutions:**
- **Zanmi Lasante / Partners in Health:** Founded by Paul Farmer and Ophelia Dahl. Operates Hôpital Bon Sauveur de Cange in Plateau Central and multiple facilities. Widely trusted in communities where they operate. They stayed. *Yo rete.* (✅ confirmed as Dieunel's reference standard — see Section 14)
- **MSF (Médecins Sans Frontières):** Major emergency medical presence, especially trauma and gang-violence treatment in Port-au-Prince
- **UNFPA, UNICEF, WHO:** Operational in Haiti with varying community trust levels
- **Faith-based facilities:** Catholic and Protestant hospitals and dispensaries in rural areas often the only formal option

📚 **Health statistics (approximate — verify before use in client deliverables):**
- Maternal mortality: among the highest in the Western Hemisphere
- Infant mortality: high; exact figures disputed
- Life expectancy: approximately 60–65 years
- HIV prevalence: historically significant; reduced through NGO programming but still elevated
- Cholera: reintroduced in 2010 by UN MINUSTAH peacekeepers from Nepal; returned in 2022 outbreak. Deeply consequential for institutional trust — UN introduced a disease that killed thousands, then denied it for years.

🔲 **Cholera/UN trust damage:** The UN introduction of cholera and its long denial is a significant institutional trust wound for Haitian communities. How individual personas carry this — especially Dieunel, Marie-Ange, Pastè Jonas — needs validation. Do not assume it is forgotten or forgiven.

📚 **2010 earthquake health legacy:**
- January 12, 2010 — 7.0 magnitude earthquake centered near Léogâne (Pastè Jonas's location)
- Estimated 160,000–316,000 deaths (widely disputed figure; Haitian government estimates were higher)
- Léogâne was among the hardest-hit zones — 80–90% of structures destroyed
- Port-au-Prince devastated
- Healthcare infrastructure destroyed; rebuilt largely by NGOs, not the state
- 15 years later, the rebuilt infrastructure is again under strain from gang displacement and collapse of governance

📚 **Mental health:**
- No formal mental health system of any scale
- Mental illness stigmatized — not universally, but significantly
- Trauma is pervasive and structurally unaddressed
- Kenzy's mental health awareness (from social media) is not matched by any service system she could access

---

## 26.4 Education

📚 **Structure:**
- Public schools exist but are severely underfunded, understaffed, and concentrated in urban areas
- The majority of schools are private — often run by churches, NGOs, or private investors
- School fees are charged even at nominally "public" institutions — this is why school fees are the central economic engine for Marie-Ange and every madan sara
- The state does not reliably provide free education — it provides the appearance of a public education system

📚 **Statistics (approximate):**
- Literacy rate: approximately 60–65% nationally; significantly lower in rural areas
- Primary enrollment: improving but incomplete
- Secondary completion: low — many Haitians (including most personas in this system) did not complete secondary school
- Tertiary: Université d'État d'Haïti (public) and multiple private universities. Kenzy attends state university.

📚 **Language of instruction:**
- Officially: French at secondary level and above, Kreyòl at primary
- Reality: many teachers and students operate in a mixed register; formal French instruction often inaccessible to students who speak only Kreyòl at home
- This creates a structural educational disadvantage that runs through class, geography, and language simultaneously

📚 **Education as class marker:**
- Completing secondary school signals upward mobility
- University degree (like Nadège's) signals elite access or significant family investment
- The family that puts a child through university is investing across generations — this is what Kenzy's enrollment means to her family

📚 **Brain drain:**
- Educated Haitians have high emigration rates — the system produces educated people who leave
- Kenzy's "bwa pi wo / grenn pwomennen" aspiration is partly this dynamic
- Haiti loses much of each educated generation to diaspora

---

## 26.5 Economy — Structural Layer

*The economic baseline (inflation, GDP contraction, gasoline prices, food insecurity, displacement figures) is already in the corpus via Section economic data. This section adds structural context.*

📚 **Informal economy:**
- Estimated 80–90% of economic activity is informal
- No reliable formal employment market — "formal jobs" are largely NGO, state, and a thin private sector
- Jèftè's situation (no stable formal employment, irregular day labor) is the norm for young men without connections, not an exception
- Cash is dominant — mobile money growing but not universal

📚 **Remittances:**
- One of the largest sources of foreign exchange — estimated at 25–40% of GDP in recent years
- Sophonie's $100–300/month is not exceptional — it is structurally expected behavior
- Remittance flows go person-to-person through: direct bank transfer, MoneyGram/Western Union, Haitian-run informal networks
- Remittances are not savings — they are consumed immediately for survival costs

📚 **The sòl (tontine / rotating savings club):**
- A centuries-old informal savings mechanism
- Members contribute a fixed amount periodically; each member receives the total "pot" in turn
- The sòl leader holds authority and manages distribution; social pressure enforces participation
- For personas without bank accounts (Marie-Ange, Jèftè), sòl is the only mechanism for accumulating capital for larger expenses
- For Nadège, Roseline, Sophonie — sòl participation is community bonding, not economic necessity, but still culturally mandatory among trusted peer groups

📚 **Agricultural sector:**
- Approximately 50–60% of the population depends on agriculture for livelihood
- Smallholder farming is the dominant mode — Dieunel is the archetype
- Artibonite Valley: primary rice-producing region; 90% of white rice commercialization runs through Madan Sara networks
- Food sovereignty is contested: Haiti imports significant quantities of rice (often subsidized US rice that undercuts local farmers — a politically sensitive history)
- Climate and environmental degradation are acute: deforestation is severe, making soil erosion, flooding, and drought worse each decade

🔲 **US rice imports and farmer consciousness:** The history of Haitian agricultural markets being disrupted by subsidized US rice (traced to 1994–1995 policies backed by IMF/World Bank) is a significant economic grievance in farming communities. Whether Dieunel carries this consciousness explicitly needs validation. Do not assume it is present or absent.

---

## 26.6 Communications & Infrastructure

📚 **Mobile phones:**
- Mobile penetration is high relative to income level — the phone is the primary digital interface for most personas
- Basic feature phones for calls and WhatsApp voice messages: Marie-Ange, Granmoun Lisette, Dieunel
- Smartphones with mobile data: Jèftè, Nadège, Kenzy, Roseline, Sophonie, Marilène
- Digicel was the dominant carrier for years; underwent bankruptcy/restructuring; service reliability variable

📚 **WhatsApp:**
- The dominant communication platform across all socioeconomic levels
- Voice messages preferred over text for lower-literacy personas
- WhatsApp groups organize: church communities (Pastè Jonas), health worker networks (Marilène), family diaspora connections (all personas), market women networks (Marie-Ange)
- WhatsApp voice notes from family are a primary news channel

📚 **Radio:**
- Remains critical, especially for rural and lower-income personas
- Battery-powered radio is the primary information source for Granmoun Lisette, Dieunel, and a backup for most others
- Trusted named programs carry weight; general broadcasts are filtered skeptically
- Radio Caraïbes, Radio Métropole: nationally known stations
- In diaspora context: Haitian radio streams online for Sophonie

📚 **Internet & social media:**
- Facebook: primary platform for news, diaspora connection, religious content, community groups
- TikTok: dominant for Gen Z (Kenzy); Haiti-specific TikTok ecosystem with its own creators and vocabulary
- Instagram: secondary for social
- YouTube: educational and entertainment content consumption
- Most internet access via mobile data — home broadband is rare outside upper-middle-class households

📚 **Electricity:**
- Unreliable national grid; outages frequent even in Port-au-Prince
- Battery banks, generators, and solar panels used by those who can afford them
- For Granmoun Lisette and Dieunel: no electricity at home
- For Marie-Ange: intermittent — the one-room compound has occasional access
- Charging phones requires planning — mobile money agents sometimes double as phone-charging stations

📚 **Roads and transportation:**
- Road network is poor, especially between departments
- Mountain roads are physically demanding and dangerous — the camion route is not a highway
- Moto-taxi is primary urban transportation in Port-au-Prince neighborhoods
- Tap-tap (shared minibuses) for urban mobility
- Airport Toussaint Louverture: closed since November 2024 — confirmed in corpus

---

## 26.7 Political & Institutional History — In Persona Consciousness

*Not academic history. What events live in these personas' memories and shape their institutional trust architecture.*

📚 **1804 — The Revolution:**
- Haiti was the first Black republic, the only successful slave revolt in history that produced a nation
- This is not distant history for Haitians — it is the founding identity claim
- *Depi nan Ginen* — "since Guinea" — proverbs reach back to before the republic
- The Citadelle Laferrière (where the stampede occurred, April 2026) was built by Henri Christophe post-independence — it is a sovereignty monument, which is part of why the stampede was not just a tragedy but felt like a desecration

📚 **US Occupation 1915–1934:**
- The United States occupied Haiti for 19 years
- American forces restructured the Haitian army, infrastructure, and economy in ways that served US interests
- This occupation is a layer in the Bouki/Ti Malice dynamic: the foreign institutional actor who comes to help and harvests the real value
- It is not ancient history — Granmoun Lisette's parents lived through it

📚 **Duvalier Era 1957–1986:**
- François "Papa Doc" Duvalier: brutal authoritarian rule 1957–1971. Tonton Macoutes paramilitary. Political terror.
- Jean-Claude "Baby Doc" Duvalier: 1971–1986. Continued repression, corruption. Fled to France in 1986.
- 29 years of the Duvalier family. Every persona over 45 has parents or grandparents who lived through this.
- The Tonton Macoute is a named cultural ghost — surveillance, informants, the neighbor who reports you
- Institutional distrust has a specific genealogy that runs through this era

📚 **Post-Duvalier instability 1986–present:**
- Series of coups, elections, canceled elections, foreign interventions
- Jean-Bertrand Aristide: elected 1990, overthrown 1991, restored by US intervention 1994, elected again 2000, forced out 2004
- René Préval, Michel Martelly, Jovenel Moïse — each representing different political networks
- The pattern: elected leaders either captured by oligarchic interests or removed before completing terms

📚 **MINUSTAH / UN Peacekeeping 1994–2017:**
- Multiple UN peacekeeping missions over three decades
- MINUSTAH (2004–2017) is the mission most present in community memory
- Introduced cholera in 2010 — confirmed link; UN denied for years, eventually acknowledged
- Multiple sexual abuse scandals involving UN peacekeepers
- The phrase "15th mission" in the Bouki corpus section refers to this cumulative history: every mission promised stabilization; none delivered it
- UN/international presence = the institutional Bouki trap for many personas

📚 **2010 Earthquake:**
- January 12, 2010. 7.0 magnitude. 35 seconds.
- Epicenter near Léogâne; Port-au-Prince devastated
- Hundreds of thousands dead; 1.5 million displaced at peak
- International response: $13 billion pledged; what reached communities is a documented governance failure
- The earthquake is the most recent civilizational rupture. Every persona over 20 was shaped by it.
- Kenzy was 5 years old. She grew up in post-earthquake Haiti.
- Marie-Ange rebuilt her market practice in post-earthquake conditions.
- The "NGO republic" critique — Haiti had more NGOs per capita than almost anywhere on earth; communities saw little of it — is widely held

📚 **Jovenel Moïse assassination — July 7, 2021:**
- President assassinated in his home by a mercenary team
- Circumstances remain partly opaque; international dimensions implicated
- Verdict in Miami federal court, May 8, 2026: 4 convicted. Who ordered it still unknown. (✅ confirmed in corpus)
- This is in active consciousness — the verdict is two days old as of session date

📚 **Gang consolidation 2021–present:**
- Following Moïse's assassination, gang networks consolidated territorial control at accelerating pace
- G9 and G-Pèp federations under figures like Jimmy "Barbecue" Chérizier (G9 leader) became major political-economic actors
- By 2024–2025: gangs controlled estimated 80%+ of Port-au-Prince territory
- The state has effectively lost the capital
- This is the operating environment for Marie-Ange (Carrefour), Jèftè (Cité Soleil), Kenzy (PaP), Nadège (Pétion-Ville), Marilène (peri-urban Ouest)

---

## 26.8 The NGO Economy — What Every Persona Knows

📚 **Scale:**
- Haiti has been described as having among the highest ratios of NGOs per capita globally, especially post-2010
- Thousands of international organizations have operated in Haiti since the earthquake
- The phrase "international community" is heard as code for: organizations that come with money, make promises, employ some local people, and leave

📚 **The pattern every persona has observed:**
1. Organization arrives, often with foreign staff
2. Assessment phase — surveys, focus groups, needs assessments
3. Implementation — often partial
4. Funding cycle ends — 18–36 months
5. Organization leaves or significantly reduces presence
6. Community is left with: sometimes infrastructure (school wall, water pump), sometimes nothing, always the memory of promises not kept

📚 **What this produces:**
- The Bouki dynamic at institutional scale: the organization extracts the data (the real harvest), community gets the leaves
- *Kay koule twonpe soley* is the primary evaluation heuristic for every persona when a new organization arrives
- *Chaloska* is the private word for organizations that perform competence and care without having it
- *"Nou konnen istwa sa a"* — We know this story — is the private summary of every new arrival

📚 **Exceptions that every persona knows:**
- Zanmi Lasante / Partners in Health: they stayed. This is exceptional enough to be the standard against which every other organization is measured.
- Organizations with 10+ year presence and community roots exist — they are the exception, not the rule

🔲 **Persona-specific NGO histories:** Which organizations have operated in each persona's specific community, and what they delivered or didn't, requires field validation. Do not name specific organizations in persona voices without confirmation.

---

## 26.9 The Diaspora Economy

📚 **Scale:**
- Haitian diaspora is estimated at 1–3 million people across the US, Canada, France, DR, Chile, Brazil
- Miami/Little Haiti: largest US concentration; Sophonie's location
- New York/Brooklyn: second largest
- Boston: significant community — relevant to Sophonie's territory and the World Cup context (Gillette Stadium, June 2026)
- Montreal: large French-speaking Haitian community

📚 **TPS (Temporary Protected Status) — US context:**
- TPS designates Haiti as a country too dangerous for deportation
- Trump administration ended TPS effective February 3, 2026 — confirmed in corpus (✅ Sophonie section)
- Approximately 500,000 Haitians face legal status change
- This is existential, not administrative, for Sophonie and the Miami Haitian community

📚 **DR deportations:**
- Dominican Republic has been deporting Haitians at high volume — 180,000+ figure in corpus
- The DR-Haiti relationship is historically complex and racially charged — anti-Haitian sentiment has a long history in the DR
- Many deportees are people who have lived in the DR for years or decades, sometimes born there

📚 **"Cage de verre" — glass cage:**
- Diaspora experience: built a life in the US/elsewhere, legally precarious, culturally between worlds
- Sophonie's *"Lakay se lakay / Lakay pa bon men lakay se lakay"* is the primary expression of this
- The cage is invisible until TPS ends, until ICE appears, until the country you built your life in decides you are deportable

---

## 26.10 Vodou — Structural Facts (Not Cultural Texture)

*Cultural texture on Vodou lives in Sections 2–10 and the persona documents. This is structural fact only.*

📚 **Legal and constitutional status:**
- Vodou was criminalized under Haitian law until 1987
- The 1987 Constitution removed the criminalization
- A 2003 decree under Aristide gave Vodou equal legal status to other religions — allowed Vodou ceremonies to be performed legally, marriages officiated by hougan and manbo to be recognized
- Despite legal recognition, social stigma persists — especially in Evangelical contexts and among educated urban elites

📚 **The attributed saying:**
- *"Haiti est 80% catholique, 20% protestant, et 100% vodouisant"* — widely cited; authorship disputed
- This is a memorable formulation of the two-layer system, not a survey result
- Evangelicals represent a growing share — the 20% Protestant figure is now likely an undercount

📚 **Post-earthquake Evangelical growth:**
- The 2010 earthquake accelerated Evangelical church growth
- Some communities interpreted the earthquake as divine judgment related to Vodou (a theological argument made explicitly by some pastors, including figures outside Haiti)
- This created both a surge in Evangelical conversion and a counter-reaction of Vodou practitioners defending their faith publicly
- Pastè Jonas's anti-Vodou theological position is more politically available to him now than it would have been 30 years ago

🔲 **How the 2010 earthquake shaped the religious landscape in each persona's specific community:** This is a significant gap. The Evangelical vs. Catholic vs. Vodou dynamic post-earthquake varies sharply by geography and community. Needs validation before use in persona voices.

---

## 26.11 Items Needing Cultural Informant Review

The following items in this section carry higher risk of being wrong, misframed, or missing important nuance. Flag for review before embedding in persona voices:

🔲 US rice imports and Dieunel's consciousness of agricultural market history
🔲 Cholera/UN trust damage — how each persona carries this
🔲 2003 Aristide Vodou decree — is this known or referenced at the community level?
🔲 Evangelical growth post-earthquake — correct proportion for each persona's geography?
🔲 Specific NGO histories in each persona's community
🔲 Tonton Macoute as a living cultural ghost — how present in contemporary speech and consciousness?
🔲 "Cage de verre" — is this the term diaspora Haitians actually use, or is this a literary formulation?
🔲 DR-Haiti relationship — beyond the structural facts, what is the affective register for each persona?

# CORPUS ADDITION — Section 26.12
## Security Situation — Current (2025–2026)
## Source: Documentary reporting + UN data

*All items 📚 unless marked. Source: documentary journalism and UN reports.*
*Append after Section 26.11 in Master Corpus.*

---

## 26.12 The Security Situation — Specific Current Data

### The Coalition: Viv Ansanm

📚 **"Viv Ansanm" ("Living Together"):**
- This is the name of the gang coalition controlling much of Port-au-Prince
- Multiple previously competing gang federations — including G9 and G-Pèp — consolidated under this alliance
- The name is deliberate irony or deliberate aspiration depending on who you ask: *living together* as a coalition of forces that have terrorized the communities they now control
- This coalition is the specific actor behind the displacement surge, the extortion networks, and the territorial control that shapes daily life for all Port-au-Prince personas

📚 **How they finance themselves:**
- Kidnappings — targeted and opportunistic
- Extortion rackets — businesses, market women, transport operators
- Marie-Ange's gang checkpoint fees are Viv Ansanm's revenue stream
- The extortion is not random. It is a system with rates, schedules, and consequences for non-payment.

📚 **Scale of violence — 2025 data:**
- Approximately 6,000 people killed by gang violence in 2025 alone (UN reports)
- This is the operating context for every Port-au-Prince persona — not background noise, not risk, not occasional event. It is the climate.
- For Jèftè in Cité Soleil: 6,000 dead in one year in a city whose entire population he knows through six degrees of connection. He has lost people. This is certain.

### What Is Being Targeted

📚 **Schools:**
- Schools are not collateral damage — they are specifically targeted in gang raids and fighting
- School closures are not administrative decisions. They are safety decisions.
- Marie-Ange's primary engine — school fees — depends on schools that may close without notice or not reopen after a raid
- This is the operational connection between gang violence and the children's education she works to protect

📚 **Healthcare facilities:**
- Clinics and hospitals remain closed or are repeatedly targeted
- Healthcare system described as "on the brink of collapse" (UN/documentary source)
- This shapes Marilène's field reality directly: the facilities she refers community members to may not be operating
- For Marie-Ange's untreated hypertension: this is not only a cost problem. It is also an access and safety problem.

📚 **Humanitarian aid:**
- Humanitarian aid reaches many Port-au-Prince neighborhoods only under considerable security risk
- Aid workers must negotiate access with gang leadership — which means gangs control who receives aid and who does not
- The Bouki dynamic at humanitarian scale: the aid that was sent for the community reaches it through the hands of the force extracting from it

### The Kenyan Mission

📚 **MMAS — Multinational Security Support Mission:**
- UN-backed; led by Kenyan police officers
- Deployed to stabilize the security situation
- Assessment as of documentary: gangs still in control in many areas of Port-au-Prince
- The mission exists. Its impact on territorial control is limited.

🔲 **How personas are experiencing the Kenyan mission:** This needs validation. What does Marie-Ange think about it? What does Jèftè think? A foreign police force in the city is not a neutral fact — it carries echoes of MINUSTAH (which introduced cholera and left), of the US occupation, of the fifteen missions. What register does "Kenyan officers" land in at the market, in Cité Soleil, in Pétion-Ville? Do not assume it is welcomed.

---

## 26.13 The Man Who Joined Viv Ansanm — The Jèftè Threshold

*This is the most analytically significant element of the documentary source.*

📚 **The documented trajectory:**
- A man in the documentary joined Viv Ansanm after years of arbitrary arrests and imprisonment
- He turned to violent crime, he says, because the state failed him
- He represents not the enemy but the produced outcome: what the system makes of a young man it arrests without cause, incarcerates without justice, and releases without support

📚 **Why this matters for Jèftè:**
This is not background context. This is Jèftè's possible future documented by a camera.

The man in the documentary was not born into the gang. He was failed into it. The sequence:
1. State engagement (arrest, imprisonment)
2. State failure (arbitrary, no justice, no support on release)
3. Institutional compression accumulates
4. One more negligence ignites it
5. The gang offers what the state never did: belonging, income, protection, respect

Jèftè has not crossed this threshold. He is adjacent to it. He knows men who crossed it. He may know men currently crossing it. He understands the logic from the inside without endorsing it — yet.

His resistance to crossing this threshold is not ideological. It is practical and relational: his mother. His aspiration for the moto. The knowledge of what it costs if it goes wrong. These are thin barriers against the compression of a system that has never offered him anything real.

**Research implication:** Any research question that touches on institutional failure, police encounters, or economic futility with Jèftè is operating near this threshold. The question "what would it take for things to change for you?" is one question away from asking him why he hasn't crossed yet. Treat it accordingly.

🔲 **Validation needed:** How Jèftè specifically thinks about the men who have joined gang structures in his neighborhood. Does he name it? Does he have people close to him who made that choice? What is the language he uses for it — if any? This territory belongs to the persona, not the researcher.

---

## 26.14 Carole — The Marie-Ange Adjacent Case

📚 **From the documentary:**
- Carole is a mother of two, now in a displaced persons camp
- She lost her home and her livelihood in a gang raid
- She represents the displacement trajectory: not a slow economic decline but a sudden, violent removal from everything

📚 **Why this matters for Marie-Ange:**
Carole is Marie-Ange's risk scenario made concrete and documented. Marie-Ange is not in a displacement camp. She is in Carrefour, which has significant gang territorial presence. The difference between her current situation and Carole's is not structural — it is positional. She is in a Carrefour that has not been raided yet, or has been raided at a level she has been able to navigate.

The displacement camp is not an abstraction for people in Marie-Ange's community. They know people who are in them. They know people who disappeared into them. The camp is the answer to the question of what happens if the gang decides this block, this compound, this market is next.

📚 **1.4 million displaced persons:**
- These are not people who left by choice
- They are people who were removed — by raids, by gun battles, by territory changes that made their neighborhood uninhabitable
- Many are in informal displacement camps on the outskirts of the areas they were expelled from
- Roseline's Cap-Haïtien is absorbing significant numbers of these people — which is already in the corpus (housing prices multiplied, food prices increased, Roseline privately tired)

---

## 26.15 Persona Impact Mapping — Security Section

| Persona | How This Section Lands | Specific |
|---|---|---|
| Marie-Ange | Viv Ansanm is the force she pays at checkpoints. The same force that killed her children's father. Carole is her risk scenario. School closures are the threat to everything she works for. | Central to daily reality |
| Jèftè | The man who joined Viv Ansanm is a person Jèftè could identify in his own network. He has not crossed that threshold. He understands why someone does. | Threshold adjacent |
| Kenzy | 6,000 dead in one year is not a statistic — it is the TikTok feed, the WhatsApp notifications, the names that come up. She has grown up scrolling through this. | Ambient trauma |
| Nadège | Writes reports about this situation. Walks through it to work. The gap between her professional language and what 6,000 dead in one year actually means has closed. | Professional and personal collision |
| Marilène | Her field visits depend on access. Aid reaching neighborhoods "under considerable security risk" is her daily calculation — which households can she reach today, which routes are open, which checkpoints are new. | Operational reality |
| Roseline | Cap-Haïtien is not Port-au-Prince. But the 1.4M displaced are arriving in her city. She is managing the consequences without having caused any of them. | Downstream effect |
| Sophonie | This is what she watches from Miami on her phone. Every UN report headline, every documentary, every WhatsApp message from family — this is what she is watching while also being told she must leave the US. | Diaspora terror |
| Granmoun Lisette | Her children are in Port-au-Prince. This is what she is praying about on the battery-powered radio. | Long-distance fear |
| Dieunel | Gangs blocking roads means his produce cannot reach market. Blocked camion routes are blocked income. He is upstream of the supply chain that Viv Ansanm is extracting from. | Supply chain disruption |
| Pastè Jonas | Léogâne is not Port-au-Prince but is close. Gang territorial expansion has been moving outward. He is watching the edge come closer. His community's security is part of his pastoral responsibility. | Peripheral but approaching |

## Vocabulary Additions for Corpus

📚 **Viv Ansanm** — "Living Together." The gang coalition controlling much of Port-au-Prince as of 2025–2026. Name used by the gangs themselves. In persona speech: never said directly, often not named at all. Known. Present. Unnamed in conversation with strangers.

📚 **Deplase** — displaced person. Someone removed from their home by gang violence and living in a camp or informal shelter elsewhere. Not a foreign word — it is how the community names what is happening.

🔲 **Validation needed:** How *deplase* is used in speech — is it self-applied? Applied by others? Does it carry stigma? Is it neutral description? This is the word for Carole. Is it the word Marie-Ange would use if she ended up in that camp, or would she refuse it?
