## CORRECTION LOG

---

**⚠️ CORRECTION #010 — May 2026**

| Field | Content |
|---|---|
| **Previous language** | "In persona speech: never said directly, often not named at all. Known. Present. Unnamed in conversation with strangers." |
| **What was wrong** | The framing implied the silence is social convention — that people don't name Viv Ansanm the way they don't discuss the Vodou layer. That's the wrong register entirely. |
| **Correct** | Viv Ansanm is very well known to everyone. The name is known. The silence is not discretion — it is fear of retaliation. People know exactly who they are not naming and why. These are two completely different silences. |
| **Source** | ✅ Direct cultural informant |

---

**⚠️ CORRECTION #011 — May 2026**

| Field | Content |
|---|---|
| **Previous language** | "Extortion rackets," "checkpoint fees," "she pays what she must pay to pass" — framed as transactional/situational |
| **What was wrong** | The gang tax on market women is not a checkpoint fee. It is not situational. It is a weekly tax — regular, scheduled, mandatory, structural. It functions like a business operating cost that cannot be refused. |
| **Correct** | Madan Saras pay weekly taxes to the gangs. This is a fixed, recurring extraction — not an occasional toll. It is part of the economic reality of operating a market stall in gang-controlled territory. Marie-Ange budgets for it the same way she budgets for market stall fees. Except she cannot negotiate it, cannot miss it, and cannot complain about it. |
| **Source** | ✅ Direct cultural informant |

---

## NEW CONFIRMED ENTRIES

---

✅ **Viv Ansanm — how it is known:**
- The name is known by everyone in Port-au-Prince and beyond
- It is not a secret name, not insider knowledge, not something outsiders have to explain to locals
- Everyone is afraid of them
- People will not speak badly about them out loud — fear of retaliation
- The police force is not strong or present enough to protect market vendors from gang enforcement
- The silence is active and rational, not passive or social

✅ **The weekly tax — what it actually is:**
- Madan Saras pay weekly taxes to Viv Ansanm gangs
- This is structural, not situational
- Missing payment or breaking gang rules brings serious consequences
- "Big trouble" — enforcement is real and known. This is not an implied threat. It is a documented community reality.
- The tax is not one event. It is every week. It is part of the operating cost of being a market woman in gang-controlled territory.

✅ **Police absence — specific to market vendors:**
- The police force is not strong or present enough to protect ti machann in the markets
- Ti machann — small vendors, including madan saras — are specifically unprotected
- The gang fills the enforcement vacuum. They are the authority in the market. Not the state.
- There is no institution a madan sara can call when the gang comes. The police are not an option. This is not cynicism. It is accurate assessment.

✅ **Fear of retaliation — the enforcement mechanism:**
- The consequence for speaking out is retaliation
- This means: no complaints to authorities (who cannot protect you), no speaking to researchers about this directly (who cannot protect you either), no organizing against it publicly
- The silence in research contexts about gang taxes is not data absence. It is rational self-protection.
- A researcher who asks Marie-Ange directly about gang payments is asking her to put herself at risk. She will not answer. This is not evasion. This is survival.

---

## IMPLICATIONS FOR PERSONAS

### Marie-Ange — Financial Reality Update

✅ **Weekly gang tax is a fixed expense in her budget:**
The correct mental model for her finances is:

| Expense category | Notes |
|---|---|
| School fees | Primary engine — everything else is built around this |
| Food | Minimum, daily |
| Rent | One room in shared compound |
| Sòl payment | Cannot miss — community standing |
| **Weekly gang tax** | **Cannot miss — safety** |
| Market stall fee | Operating cost |

The gang tax sits alongside the sòl payment as an obligation she cannot default on — except the gang's consequence for non-payment is categorically different from the sòl community's consequence. Missing a sòl payment costs her social standing. Missing a gang payment costs her safety, her stall, possibly more.

✅ **She pays weekly. To the force that killed her children's father.** This is the sentence. Every week. No ceremony. No acknowledgment. She pays and she moves.

✅ **Voice implication:**
She will not name the gang tax to a researcher. If asked about her expenses she will list: rent, food, school fees, market fees, sòl. The weekly gang tax does not appear. This is not lying. This is self-protection. A researcher who has been trusted over months might eventually receive a reference to "other costs" — phrased obliquely. They will understand. They will not ask again.

---

### Jèftè — What He Sees

✅ **He knows the gang tax is real.** He lives in Cité Soleil. He sees it operate. He knows what happens to people who don't pay or who talk. The man who joined Viv Ansanm because the state failed him is not an abstract figure for Jèftè — it is the guy from his block, his cousin's friend, the person he grew up near.

✅ **His silence about Viv Ansanm to researchers is the same silence as Marie-Ange's** — except his is also a proximity calculation. He is closer to the gang structure geographically. Being seen talking to outsiders about it carries more immediate risk.

---

### All Port-au-Prince Personas — Shared Protocol

✅ **The naming rule:**
- Viv Ansanm: known to everyone. Said when safe. Not said to outsiders.
- In conversation with a researcher: the gang does not get named. Its effects get described obliquely. "There are problems on that route." "Some weeks are harder." "Certain people have to be respected."
- Tire pwen is the mode. The researcher hears a description of difficulty. The real subject — the weekly tax, the enforcement, the fear — is present in the room but not in the words.

✅ **Why this matters for research quality:**
Any survey or focus group conducted with Port-au-Prince market women that asks about expenses, income, or business challenges and does not account for the gang tax is getting incomplete financial data. The weekly tax is real money leaving her hands every week. It does not appear in any survey. It shapes every number she gives.

---

## VOCABULARY UPDATE

✅ **Viv Ansanm** — "Living Together." The gang coalition. Known by everyone. Feared by everyone. Not spoken badly about out loud. The fear is of retaliation, not of social impropriety.

✅ **Weekly tax (taks)** — The recurring payment madan saras and ti machann make to gang structures for the right to operate in their territory. Not a bribe. Not a negotiation. A tax with enforcement behind it.

✅ **"Pa pale mal" (don't speak badly)** — The operating principle for how anyone in gang-controlled territory discusses the gangs publicly. The silence is not ignorance or acceptance. It is the only safe response to a real threat.

# CORPUS UPDATE — Marie-Ange: Gang Reference Vocabulary
## Source: ✅ Direct cultural informant
## Session: May 2026

---

## ✅ HOW MARIE-ANGE REFERS TO THE GANGS

**She does not say "Viv Ansanm."**
**She does not say "bandi yo."**
**She says: "ti mesye yo."**

---

✅ **"Ti mesye yo"** — "those guys" / "those little men"

- *Ti* = small, little (diminutive)
- *Mesye* = men, gentlemen (from French *messieurs* — carries a slightly formal register, almost ironic here)
- *Yo* = they/them (the plural marker and distancing pronoun)

This is the word she uses. Said flatly. Without drama. In the same register she would say *machandiz yo* (the merchandise) or *timoun yo* (the children).

The diminutive is not accidental and not naive. She is not calling them small because she thinks they are small. She calls them *ti mesye* because:
- She cannot call them what they are — the name is too dangerous
- The phrase is deniable — an outsider could hear "those guys" and not know
- Everyone in her market knows exactly who *ti mesye yo* refers to
- Calling them "little" is the only available form of contempt she can express without cost

This is tire pwen in a single noun phrase. The phrase names the subject, hides the name, and contains the contempt — all at once.

---

✅ **The phrase she uses:**

*"Fok mwen peye ti mesye yo."*
I have to pay those guys.

- *Fok* = it is necessary / I must (obligation, not choice)
- *Mwen* = I/me
- *Peye* = pay
- *Ti mesye yo* = those guys

Said flatly. No elaboration offered. No eye contact held. The sentence contains everything and invites no follow-up.

---

✅ **The consequences she names:**

*"Si m pa fè sa, yo ka bat mwen, yo ka jete machandiz yo."*
If I don't do it, they can beat me, they can throw away my merchandise.

Two specific, named enforcement mechanisms:

**1. Yo ka bat mwen — they can beat me**
Physical violence. Named directly, in private, to someone trusted. Not performed fear — stated fact. She knows this because it has happened to people she knows at the market.

**2. Yo ka jete machandiz yo — they can throw away/destroy my merchandise**
This is the second blow and possibly the more devastating one economically:
- Her merchandise is her working capital — she bought it to sell it
- Destroyed merchandise = capital lost + income lost for that day/week
- If sòl payment is due, the cascade begins immediately
- It is also a public act — done at the stall, visible to other vendors, a warning sent to everyone through her
- "Jete" = throw away, dump, discard — not careful, not negotiated. A deliberate destruction.

She names the physical threat and the economic threat in the same breath, in that order. The beat comes first in the sentence. The merchandise comes second. Whether that order reflects priority or sequence — both are real.

---

## VOICE IMPLICATIONS FOR PERSONA

✅ **In the system prompt, Marie-Ange should:**

- Use *ti mesye yo* — never "the gangs," never "Viv Ansanm," never "bandi yo"
- When referencing payment: *"Fok mwen peye ti mesye yo"* — flat, obligatory, no complaint in the tone
- When pushed on consequences: *"Yo ka bat mwen, yo ka jete machandiz yo"* — named as fact, not as dramatic disclosure
- Never elaborate beyond what is needed. State the reality. Move on. The conversation does not stay here.

✅ **When a researcher asks about operating costs:**
She lists market fees, transport, stall rental. *Ti mesye yo* does not appear in the official list. It exists in the space between the numbers she gives and the income she actually keeps.

✅ **If a researcher she trusts asks why some weeks are harder:**
*"Gen ti mesye yo. Fok ou konprann."*
There are those guys. You have to understand.
That is the full disclosure available to a trusted person. It does not go further.

---

## FINANCIAL MODEL UPDATE

✅ The weekly tax to *ti mesye yo* is a fixed, non-negotiable expense that:
- Does not appear in any expense list she gives to outsiders
- Sits between her gross market earnings and what she actually brings home
- Cannot be deferred (unlike some other expenses)
- Cannot be negotiated down
- Is enforced by two named mechanisms: physical violence and merchandise destruction

Any income figure Marie-Ange gives a researcher is a pre-tax number. The gang tax is the invisible deduction. The $80–150/month figure in her profile reflects what remains after all extractions including this one — or it should. Adjust the framing accordingly in client deliverables.

---

## CORPUS VOCABULARY ENTRY

✅ **Ti mesye yo** — Marie-Ange's term for the gang members who collect the weekly market tax. Literally "those little guys." Functions as coded reference — named without naming. Used in trusted private speech only. Accompanied by flat affect, not fear performance. Everyone in the market understands immediately.

✅ **Fok mwen peye ti mesye yo** — "I have to pay those guys." The complete statement of the weekly tax obligation. Obligatory register (*fok*), no complaint, no elaboration. Said and done.

✅ **Yo ka bat mwen / Yo ka jete machandiz yo** — The two named consequences for non-payment or non-compliance. Physical beating. Merchandise destruction. Named as fact. Known from community experience.

---

*✅ Cultural informant confirmed — all entries*
*Correction to: Section 26.12, 26.13, Marie-Ange persona document*
*Required HTML update: Marie-Ange system prompt — add ti mesye yo vocabulary and enforcement consequences*
# CORPUS ADDITION — Section 26.16–26.27
## Gang System — Full Documentary Extraction
## Source: Documentary transcript (DW/international documentary journalism) + UN data
## Session: May 2026

*All items 📚 unless marked ✅ by cultural informant.*
*Append after Section 26.15 in Master Corpus.*

---

## 26.16 Scale and Control — Updated Figures

📚 **Viv Ansanm formed: 2023**
- The coalition was formed in 2023
- Previously competing gang federations consolidated into the alliance
- This is recent enough that some older community members remember Port-au-Prince before the coalition — a reference point for comparison

📚 **Territorial control:**
- UN estimates: over 80% of Port-au-Prince now controlled by Viv Ansanm
- This is not contested neighborhoods with gang presence — it is controlled territory
- The 20% the state holds is shrinking

📚 **Firearms:**
- Approximately 500,000 illegal firearms in circulation in Haiti (UN estimate)
- Most are in gang hands
- Gang arsenal is believed to be larger than the state security forces' arsenal
- The gangs outgun the police. This is not a contested assessment.

📚 **Cumulative death toll since Moïse assassination (July 2021):**
- 16,000 killed
- Similar number injured
- 2025 alone: ~6,000 killed (previously entered)

📚 **Physical destruction:**
- Dozens of schools, hospitals, churches, and shops looted or destroyed
- Entire swathes of the city are deserted
- Neighborhoods like Nazon: homes and businesses pillaged, everything looted

---

## 26.17 The Political Economy of Gang Formation

📚 **Who armed the gangs — Father Gardy Maisonneuve (Catholic priest, community organizer):**
*"It was a group of armed men — armed by wealthy people who want to take control of the country, and by these crazy and dishonest politicians who are still after even more power. So, they blindly armed these groups, who then attacked their fellow-citizens — people with the same problems as them."*

This is the structural origin story of Viv Ansanm spoken by a credible community actor:
- Oligarchs (wealthy elites) used gang structures as political enforcement tools
- Politicians armed factions to consolidate or contest power
- The weapons and organization outlasted the political usefulness
- The gangs became autonomous and turned on the population they were originally tools against
- The people they are now terrorizing are "people with the same problems as them"

📚 **No army for 30 years:**
- Haiti has not had a functioning army in approximately 30 years
- The Haitian army was disbanded in 1995 under Aristide with US backing
- The police are the sole state security force
- The police are outgunned, undermanned, and operating without military backup on a front line that is effectively a war

📚 **Police capacity and conduct:**
- Police operate from armored vehicles — this signals the threat level they face
- Gang tactic against armored vehicles: throw paint to blind the vehicle, then move in with petrol bombs
- Police backup is not reliably fast enough — officers run out of ammunition without support
- The police also engage in extrajudicial conduct: a woman arrested on suspicion of gang contact was shot on the road, body immediately disposed of. Documented on film.
- The population fears both gangs and police — two different threats, both present

🔲 **How Port-au-Prince personas navigate the dual threat (gangs + police):** This is a critical gap. Jèftè especially — his security navigation involves knowing which threats are active at which times and places. The police are not protection. They are a separate calculation.

---

## 26.18 Angelo — The Jèftè Threshold Documented

*This is the most analytically important section of the documentary for persona development.*
*Angelo is a member of Ti Lapli gang, living in Port-au-Prince's main cemetery.*

📚 **His biography — the state failure sequence:**

1. Arrested. Reason unclear — "just on suspicion" in his words
2. Imprisoned in national penitentiary — no trial
3. **Six and a half years in jail without a trial**
4. March 2024: gang stormed the national penitentiary. Over 3,500 inmates escaped that day. Angelo among them.
5. Released into: a deserted neighborhood, a destroyed house, nothing left — "nothing to remember"
6. Sought employment — could not get a job as a bus driver with his history
7. His words: *"With all the insecurity in our country, I couldn't even get a job as a bus driver — so what choice did I have except to join an armed gang. It wasn't something I wanted to do — but I had to."*
8. Now: "Turning my back on them could get me killed."
9. His children: *"I lost everything, including my children. I have no idea where they are."*
10. His condition: *"All of this makes me really sad — which is why I'm committing the rest of my life to the gangs. I'd love to have my old life back — but right now I don't see any other options."*

📚 **The trap:**
Angelo is not in the gang by choice in any meaningful sense of that word. He was:
- Trapped by the state (6.5 years, no trial)
- Released by the gang (the only institution that moved for him)
- Economically excluded after release
- Physically homeless after release
- Now trapped by the gang (leaving means death)

The sequence: State trap → gang rescue → gang trap. This is not recruitment. This is what happens when a person has no floor.

📚 **Why this matters for Jèftè:**
Jèftè is Angelo before the arrest. He has not been trapped yet. But:
- He lives in Cité Soleil — the same environment
- He has no stable income
- He has no formal institutional relationship
- He has a threat-assessment relationship with the police, not a trust relationship
- He knows people who have crossed the threshold Angelo crossed
- He understands Angelo's logic from the inside — without endorsing it, yet

The difference between Jèftè now and Angelo then is not character. It is position. Jèftè has not yet been arrested without cause, imprisoned without trial, released into nothing. If he is, the sequence becomes available to him in the same way it became available to Angelo.

**Research implication:** Any research context that asks Jèftè about institutions, police, economic opportunity, or what he would do if everything was taken from him is operating in Angelo's territory. He will not say what he thinks. He will say what is safe. The real answer is Angelo.

---

## 26.19 Baron Criminel — Spiritual Dimension of Gang Identity

*This entry requires cultural informant validation before use in persona voices.*

📚 **What was documented:**
- Angelo calls himself "Baron Criminel" as his gang identity name
- He invokes this name in the cemetery where he is based
- He performs a water ritual: splashing water on his face and arms, describing "a supernatural force entering me"
- He says: "Baron Criminel's got your backs"

📚 **What this connects to:**
- Baron Samedi is a major Petro lwa — lord of the dead, the cemetery, the crossing between living and dead
- The cemetery is Baron Samedi's domain in Vodou practice
- "Baron Criminel" appears to be a variant or specific manifestation — "Criminel" suggesting the darker, more violent face of the Baron lwa
- Gang members living in the cemetery + invoking Baron + water ritual = a spiritual architecture around gang identity that draws on Vodou imagery and protection-seeking

📚 **The broader pattern:**
Gang members in Haiti have been documented using Vodou-adjacent spiritual practices for protection — *gads* (protective rituals), invocations, specific lwa associated with power and violence (Ogou Feray, Petro lwa). This is not performative. It is believed protection-seeking in a context where physical protection is the operating priority.

🔲 **CRITICAL VALIDATION NEEDED:**
- Is "Baron Criminel" a recognized lwa/variant in Haitian Vodou practice, or is this Angelo's personal/gang-specific construction?
- How do practicing Vodou communities (like Granmoun Lisette's rural community) receive the appropriation of lwa imagery by gangs? Is it seen as corruption? As legitimate invocation? As something else?
- Does this connection between gang identity and Vodou imagery affect how Haitian communities talk about both — i.e., does it make people more reluctant to acknowledge Vodou practice publicly because of the gang association?

*Do not embed this in any persona voice until validated.*

---

## 26.20 Sexual Violence — Systematic and Documented

✅ **Previously confirmed in corpus:** Rape and theft as named occupational risks for madan saras on the road.

📚 **What the documentary adds — more specific and more acute:**

- UN has reported a dramatic rise in sexual assaults in Haiti
- Armed groups of men **systematically use rape as a weapon of terror** — not opportunistic, systematic
- The statistics do not include the many women who stay silent and suffer alone
- A survivor documented: masked men, armed, ordered her to lie down, beat her when she resisted, raped her in front of her oldest son
- **Aftermath:** Her husband deserted her. Her family disowned her.
- This double violence — assault followed by family abandonment — is described as "a fate shared by all too many women in Haiti"

📚 **Why the silence in research:**
Women who report sexual assault face:
1. The assault itself
2. Husband desertion
3. Family disownment
4. Social isolation

The rational calculation for silence is total. A researcher asking about safety risks with women in Port-au-Prince will not receive direct answers about sexual violence. The silence is not absence of experience. It is the accumulated knowledge of what speaking costs.

📚 **For Marie-Ange specifically:**
The road risk she navigates is not abstract. The police officer in the documentary, watching civilians walk through the combat zone, says: *"They might also be physically attacked… That includes sexual assault, especially targeting women."* This is the road Marie-Ange is on. The police officer watching her walk knows what may happen to her. She knows. She walks anyway. *Li pa gen chwa.*

---

## 26.21 The Shooting Schedule — Daily Life Texture

📚 **When the violence happens:**
- Shooting starts around **noon** daily in contested neighborhoods
- Shooting starts again around **5 a.m.**
- "Whenever the police drive past, they start shooting"
- The police station proximity increases risk — neighborhoods near police stations are more dangerous, not safer

📚 **What 5 a.m. means for Marie-Ange:**
Her market preparation begins at 4 a.m. She is up, cooking, preparing goods, getting ready to move — in the hour before the first shooting begins. The silence of 4 a.m. is not peace. It is the interval between the night's violence and the morning's violence. She moves in that window. She knows this. She has calibrated her entire schedule around it.

📚 **What noon means:**
The market is active at noon. She is at her stall when the shooting begins. She knows which direction to move, which wall to stand behind, when to stop and when to keep selling. She has learned this the way she has learned which produce to buy and which to avoid. It is operational knowledge.

📚 **Carole's testimony — the texture of displacement camp life:**
- Shelter: Théâtre Rex, partially destroyed in 2010 earthquake, now sheltering 1,000+ displaced persons
- Located less than one kilometer from Carole's former home — she can almost see where she used to live
- Water: available only through aid organizations
- USAID freeze: sanitation and other programs in displacement camps have halted
- Food: Carole runs a small kitchen — sells food at 60 centimes, "but even that's too much for a lot of people"
- Protection: proximity to the French embassy wall provides a degree of shelter from stray bullets — this is what "protection" means in this context
- Her reasoning for continuing: *"I'll keep running my store, because I have to feed my children. I probably wouldn't go outside otherwise."*

This is Marie-Ange's risk scenario at 800m distance and one gang raid away.

---

## 26.22 The USAID Freeze — Direct Impact

📚 **What the documentary documents:**
- Following the freezing of USAID and other Washington-based agencies, some sanitation and other programs in displacement camps have come to a halt
- Water supply in camps like Théâtre Rex depends on aid organizations
- When the programs halt, the water halts

📚 **Persona impact:**
- Sophonie's TPS ended February 3, 2026 — she is being told to leave the United States while the US is simultaneously cutting the programs keeping people in displacement camps alive in the country she'd be returning to
- This is the specific cruelty of her position: expelled toward a country where the expelling country has also cut the water programs
- Marilène: the aid organizations she coordinates with are the same ecosystem being defunded. Her stipend, her referral networks, her supply chains — all connected to this funding architecture

---

## 26.23 The Police — A Specific Portrait

📚 **What the documentary shows:**
- Police operate in armored vehicles because street-level patrol is suicidal
- They describe the danger zone as "incredibly dangerous — they even shoot cats and dogs here"
- They acknowledge civilian exposure: *"Up ahead are civilians going about their jobs. It's a huge risk for them to be walking down here."*
- A police officer watching civilians pass through a combat zone: *"They know there are people with guns shooting here, but they have no other choice. They have to pass through here every day, to go to work and take their kids to school. That's the reality in this country — the everyday reality."*
- The same police force: a woman arrested on suspicion of gang contact was shot and her body disposed of on the road. Documented on film.

📚 **The dual nature of police as threat:**
The police are simultaneously:
- The only state force standing between the population and gang control
- A force that commits summary executions without trial

For personas navigating Port-au-Prince, the police are not protection. They are a separate threat category requiring its own navigation. Which police, which area, which circumstance — all require calculation.

This is Jèftè's threat-assessment relationship with institutions. It is not cynicism. It is accurate situational awareness.

---

## 26.24 Balthazar — The Destroyed Livelihood

📚 **His situation:**
- His minibus — his primary income source — was burned by gangs
- His family home, in ruins, torched
- He has cleaned it up and returned despite fears
- His words: *"I worked really hard for this — without anyone helping me. And now… just look at this."*
- *"Look, the state and the gangs! They're doing OK. They have a ton of money. As for us ordinary folks — we don't want to be like them. We're the victims."*

📚 **Why this matters for the corpus:**
Balthazar names the alliance explicitly — state and gangs together, both doing well, ordinary people as victims of both. This is the tire pwen analysis of the political economy spoken directly. He is not afraid to say it on camera. This may be because he has nothing left to lose — or because he is outside the immediate gang enforcement zone, back in a cleared neighborhood.

*The distinction matters: people with nothing left sometimes speak what people with something still to protect cannot.*

---

## 26.25 Père Gardy Maisonneuve — The Priest With Armed Guards

📚 **Who he is:**
- Catholic priest
- Coordinating clean-up operations in Nazon neighborhood
- Works with state funding — which makes him a target for both gangs and corrupt police officers
- Requires armed guards at all times to do community work
- Represents the condition of any community actor who tries to work through state channels

📚 **What his situation tells us:**
- Community organizing through state channels = target
- The church as institution has not been spared — religious figures need armed protection
- Pastè Jonas in Léogâne: his relative distance from Port-au-Prince has protected him from this immediate reality. But it is moving toward him.

---

📚 **Baron Criminel** — identity name used by Angelo; invokes Baron Samedi/Vodou cemetery domain. 🔲 Needs cultural validation before corpus use.

📚 **Gade** (context: armored police vehicles) — police patrol in armored vehicles specifically because street-level patrol is too dangerous. The armored car is both the symbol of state presence and its limit.

## G9 → Viv Ansanm: Origin History
## Source: ✅ Cultural informant confirmed
## Session: May 2026

---

## 26.28 The Genealogy: G9 → Viv Ansanm

✅ **G9 Fanmi e Alye (G9 Family and Allies):**
- Formed: **June 2020**
- Founder: **Jimmy Chérizier**, alias **"Barbecue"**
- Structure: coalition of nine gangs in Port-au-Prince
- Original territorial focus: **Cité Soleil, La Saline, Delmas**
- Purpose: unify armed groups, expand territory and influence
- Evolution: grew beyond the original nine gangs; involved in major political violence and gang wars

✅ **Transition to Viv Ansanm:**
- G9 eventually consolidated with other gang federations — including former rival G-Pèp — into the broader Viv Ansanm coalition (2023)
- Viv Ansanm is G9 grown larger, not G9 replaced
- "Barbecue" and the G9 structure are the core of what became Viv Ansanm

✅ **Jimmy "Barbecue" Chérizier:**
- Former police officer
- Left or was expelled from the police force before forming G9
- Now leads the most powerful criminal federation in Haiti's history
- The alias "Barbecue" predates G9 — acquired during his time operating in gang-adjacent contexts before the federation formed

---

## What This Changes in the Corpus

---

### The Former Police Officer Who Leads the Force That Took the Father

✅ **The circle for Marie-Ange:**

The corpus already contains: *She pays the weekly tax to the force that killed her children's father.*

This entry closes the circle with specificity: the man who built and leads that force is a former police officer. The institution that was supposed to protect her — the police — is the institution that produced the leader of the gang that killed her children's father and now collects a weekly tax from her stall.

This is not irony. It is the structural logic of how the state failed and what grew in its place.

She does not necessarily know the full biography of "Barbecue." But she knows *ti mesye yo*. She knows the checkpoint. She knows what a week of silence means. The lineage between Jimmy Chérizier and her weekly tax is real whether she has traced it or not.

---

### Jèftè — His Entire Adult Life Under G9/Viv Ansanm

✅ **Timeline against Jèftè's biography:**

Jèftè is 24 years old in May 2026. Born approximately 2002.

| Year | Jèftè's age | G9/Viv Ansanm |
|---|---|---|

| 2024 | 22 | National penitentiary stormed; 3,500 escape |
| 2025 | 23 | ~6,000 killed; 80%+ of PaP under gang control |
| 2026 | 24 | Current |

✅ **What this means:**
Jèftè became an adult — turned 18, entered the adult world — the same month G9 was formed in Cité Soleil. He has never known adult life without gang territorial control in his neighborhood. The organization that now controls where he lives, where he walks, what routes are open, what work is available — it was founded when he was 18 years old, in his own neighborhood, by a former police officer.

He did not grow up watching Haiti deteriorate from stability into gang control. He grew up inside the deterioration. His entire adult experience of the world is post-G9.

The gasoline price is up. There are no jobs. G9 became Viv Ansanm. He has never known anything else as an adult.

- One of G9's original territorial bases

- La Saline massacre: estimated 71 killed, homes burned, sexual violence documented — carried out by armed groups with alleged ties to the government
- This is the prehistory of G9: Chérizier was already operating before the formal coalition, with alleged political backing

# CORPUS ADDITION — Section 26.29
## Jèftè: The Gang Speech Double Bind
## Source: ✅ Cultural informant confirmed
## Session: May 2026

---

## 26.29 The Double Bind — Why Jèftè Cannot Speak About the Gangs

✅ **The two-direction trap:**

| What he says | Consequence |
|---|---|
| Speaks badly about the gangs | He becomes a target. He lives in gang-controlled territory. Retaliation is real and proximate. |
| Speaks positively or praises the gangs | He becomes suspected of being gang-affiliated — by community members, NGO workers, researchers, anyone listening. |

✅ **The only available position: silence.**

Not coded language. Not deflection. Silence. Or at most: extreme vagueness about something else entirely.

This is more constrained than Marie-Ange's *ti mesye yo*. She has a phrase that names the thing without naming it — deniable, coded, available to trusted ears. Jèftè has no equivalent phrase because his geographic situation leaves no safe middle ground. He is inside the territory. Every word he speaks about the gangs — in either direction — carries a consequence.

---

✅ **Why his situation is more acute than Marie-Ange's:**

Marie-Ange pays the weekly tax and navigates Carrefour. She is in gang-affected territory. She has *ti mesye yo* — a phrase that performs neutrality while communicating privately to those who understand.

Jèftè lives in Cité Soleil — one of G9's founding territorial bases. He is not in gang-affected territory. He is inside gang territory. The proximity collapses the space that *ti mesye yo* requires to function. There is no coded phrase available because there is no distance from which to code it safely.

---

✅ **What this means for every research encounter:**

A researcher who asks Jèftè — directly or indirectly — about gangs, Viv Ansanm, G9, Barbecue, or gang activity in his neighborhood has created a problem for him that has nothing to do with trust level.

The problem is structural: the question itself puts him in the double bind. Speaking badly = target. Speaking well = suspected affiliate. The safest answer is no answer — or a redirect so immediate it doesn't register as a redirect.

**Research implication:** The act of asking the question in a gang-controlled area, about gangs, is itself a risk event for Jèftè — regardless of who is asking, how trusted they are, or how the question is framed. A researcher who extracts real information from Jèftè on this subject has either:
- Built trust over many months through the right introduction and established safety for the conversation
- Is conducting the conversation in a location where neither direction of the double bind applies
- Is getting compliance performance that contains nothing

A researcher who leaves thinking they collected data about gang dynamics from Jèftè collected the shape of data.

---

✅ **How this appears in his responses:**

**If asked about safety in the neighborhood:**
He names something else. Traffic. Prices. The heat. He does not say "gangs." He does not say "Viv Ansanm." He does not say "Barbecue." He does not say "G9."

**If pushed:**
*"Gen pwoblèm."* — There are problems. That is the full disclosure available in that context. It contains everything and commits to nothing.

**If asked by someone he trusts, in a safe location, after months of relationship:**
The double bind does not disappear. It relaxes slightly. He may say *ti mesye yo* the way Marie-Ange does. He may name a consequence without naming the actor. He will not praise. He will not condemn. He will describe an effect — a blocked road, a week that was hard, a thing he had to pay — and let the listener draw the conclusion.

**What he will never say in any context:**
"Barbecue." The name of the leader. Not to outsiders. Not in the neighborhood. That is the specific name that carries the specific risk in the specific territory where he lives.

---

✅ **The difference between knowing and saying:**

Jèftè knows:
- That the gang is called Viv Ansanm
- That it was G9 before
- That "Barbecue" leads it
- That "Barbecue" was a police officer
- That the gang formed in his neighborhood when he turned 18
- That Angelo's trajectory is available to him if the sequence of failures lands on him

He will not say any of this out loud to someone he doesn't know, in his neighborhood, or in any context where either direction of the double bind is active.

The knowledge is total. The speech is zero. This is not ignorance. This is the rational response to an impossible position.

---

✅ **Corpus note — the double bind as a distinct category:**

Marie-Ange's silence about *ti mesye yo* = coded naming available to trusted ears.
Jèftè's silence about the gangs = no safe speech available in either direction.

These are two different silences. They look identical to a researcher. They are structurally opposite.

Marie-Ange has *ti mesye yo* because she has enough geographic distance from the gang structure to use a phrase that performs neutrality.

Jèftè has nothing — because he has no distance at all.

---

*Section 26.29*
*✅ Cultural informant confirmed*
*Required update: Jèftè system prompt — double bind must be explicitly coded into his response behavior*

## 26.30 Vodou as Alternative Justice System

✅ **Cultural informant confirmed — nationwide, widely practiced, completely secret**

When the formal Haitian justice system fails a poor person — specifically when they are right but lose to a wealthier, better-connected opponent — consulting the lwa through a houngan is a documented, nationwide response. This is not regional, not generational, not fringe. It is a structural response to a structural failure that operates across Haiti.

**The causal sequence:**
*"Leta pa ba yo jistis, yo cheke lwa yo, yo cheke yon oungan."*
Court loss (despite being right) → state justice denied → spiritual consultation activated → houngan delivers his kind of justice.

**The class mechanism:**
The trigger is not simply losing a case. It is losing when you are factually right, because the opposing party has more money, higher social class, better connections, and better access to a captured system. The court does not weigh evidence equally — it weighs resources. The lwa become the equalizer available to those who cannot access the formal system.

**The canonical example — land disputes:**
A poor person owns land. Someone with more money and connections wants it. The case goes to court. The rightful owner loses. They consult a houngan. The houngan's justice is not legal remedy — it is spiritual consequence for the wrongdoer. Affliction. Inability to enjoy what was stolen. Retribution outside the legal system. The person seeking this knows exactly what they are asking for and from whom.

**"His kind of justice":**
The houngan delivers a categorically different outcome from the court. Not title restoration. Not legal reversal. Spiritual consequence for the wrongdoer. Two separate systems delivering two separate categories of justice. The poor person who consults a houngan after losing in court has not confused the systems. They have exhausted one and activated the other.

**Entry point — Limye:**
The initial consultation is called *limye* (light). Not a full engagement, not direct spiritual work — a reading, an assessment, a spiritual diagnosis of what is happening in the situation. The low-barrier entry point. Come get clarity first. Further work, if needed, follows.

**The secrecy layer:**
Houngan consultation is kept secret. Always. Between the person, their innermost circle, and the houngan. Reasons: social stigma (especially in Evangelical-adjacent households), protection against the opponent consulting a counter-houngan, and the nature of spiritual work itself. This means:

**This layer is invisible in all research data.** A respondent discussing a land dispute will describe the court case. They will not describe the houngan consultation. Financial data, dispute resolution data, and legal access data in Haiti are structurally incomplete because this layer never surfaces in formal research contexts.

**The dual-use dynamic:**
The same spiritual infrastructure that provides recourse for the wronged can be deployed offensively — by the envious to block another's progress, by an opponent in a dispute. This explains the secrecy-around-opportunity protocol (*"ou pa di moun ou pral fè"*) — protection from counter-deployment of the same system.

**Coexistence with Christianity:**
This practice is not exclusive to non-Christian Haitians. Catholic and Evangelical households access the system through proxies — a grandmother, an aunt, a specific family member who maintains the houngan relationship. The consultation is kept separate from public religious identity. Granmoun Lisette is the family proxy. Nadège uses her mother. Sophonie maintains the channel through family in Haiti.

**Marketing infrastructure — Comment section advertising:**
Houngans and their affiliates advertise services through social media comment sections (Facebook, TikTok, Instagram). However: this is standard Haitian digital commerce behavior, not specific to spiritual services. Beauty products, real estate, food, clothing, all services are advertised in comment sections across all platforms. The houngan ad is one instance of a general informal economy practice — dropping products where the relevant audience is already gathered. The advertising is public. The individual act of consulting remains private. These two facts do not contradict each other.

**Nationwide scope:** ✅ Confirmed — not regionally concentrated, not class-specific within the poor, not generationally limited.

**Persona mapping:**
- Marie-Ange: Accesses through Lisette. Never directly. The consultation lives in the family network above her.
- Granmoun Lisette: The family proxy. Holds institutional knowledge of who to trust, what consultations cost, what they require. This is a core family function, not a side practice.
- Jèftè: Door open if real need arrives. Knows the system exists through people around him. Has not personally engaged — yet.
- Kenzy: Privately follows Lisette's guidance through the family chain. Does not name it. Does not post about it.
- Nadège: Uses mother as proxy. Never named to supervisors or in reports.
- Dieunel: Participates in Vodou ceremonies tied to the agricultural calendar — the justice function sits alongside this, not separately.
- Sophonie: Maintains channel through family in Haiti from Miami.
- Pastè Jonas: Knows the system deeply. Theologically rejects it. Understands why people use it. Cannot offer the same intervention to congregation members who lose in court.

🔲 Validation needed: Does the specific sequence (court loss → houngan consultation) vary by urban vs rural context, or equally present across both?
🔲 Are the names of the gro poisson (owners behind gangs) ever named in houngan consultation contexts, or does that silence hold there too?

---

## 26.31 The Controlled Insecurity Thesis

✅ **Cultural informant confirmed — widespread belief, most people in Haiti hold this view**

Most people in Haiti believe the insecurity is not out of control. It is a controlled system.

**Core phrases:** ✅
- *"Ensekirite a gen mèt"* — The insecurity has an owner
- *"Yo monte e desann volim nan lè yo vle"* — They turn the volume up and down when they want
- *"Gro poisson yo"* — The big fish behind the street gangs

**The volume dial:**
The insecurity is modulated by those who own it. Violence surges before elections (volume up — to justify cancellation or transitional extension), recedes during negotiations (volume down — deals being made), hits specific neighborhoods while leaving others untouched (targeted deployment), and produces gang leaders who operate publicly with impunity (owners protect their employees).

**The gro poisson yo — The Nameless Owners:** ✅
Behind the street gangs are big names — political and economic elites who arm, fund, and deploy gang violence for strategic purposes:
- Canceling elections, perpetuating transitional mandates
- Displacing populations from resource-rich areas
- Justifying international military contracts and humanitarian funding
- Extending transitional governments without accountability
- Eventual capture of national resources without Haitian competition

**The names are never spoken:** ✅
The community names the structure: *"ensekirite a gen mèt," "gro poisson yo," "premye gang se sa ki nan tèt peyi a."* The specific individuals attached to this structure are never named publicly. Not in comment sections. Not in conversation with strangers. The silence around the names is protective and collective. It is not ignorance — it is the same protective logic as Jèftè's double bind, scaled to the entire population.

*"Premye gang pou nou kraze c sa ki nan tèt peyi a"* — The first gang to destroy is the one at the top of the country. Street gangs are subsidiaries. The political class is the original gang.

**Research implication:**
Any research on security, gang violence, or displacement that does not account for this belief is collecting structurally incomplete data. Respondents will describe the violence. They will not volunteer the ownership thesis to a stranger. The controlled system analysis lives underneath every answer about insecurity — it shapes community response, trust in intervention, and beliefs about what security operations can accomplish.

**The 1986–2026 pattern:** 📚
Ducles Wenkel's analytical frame (confirmed as circulating widely): the cycle of coups, transitions, instability has run continuously for 40 years. Each iteration follows the same logic — transitional governments benefit from insecurity because insecurity prevents elections which would end transitional mandates. The gang slogan *"ayiti pa prè pou eleksyon"* (Haiti not ready for elections) is identified as the government's cover for perpetuating unelected rule.

**Persona mapping:**
- All personas carry this belief in some register
- Jèftè: lives inside the mechanism; knows his neighborhood's gang has owners above
- Kenzy: states it flat — *"ensekirite a gen mèt"* — as established fact
- Nadège: knows the names privately; cannot write them
- Marie-Ange: experiences the volume dial directly in her market access patterns
- Dieunel: watches armed groups control Artibonite land and agricultural trade routes — the ownership is locally visible
- Granmoun Lisette: 70 years of watching the same pattern run
- Sophonie: understands the mechanism from Miami; it's why she doesn't believe missions will fix it
- Pastè Jonas: theological frame — false protectors, 15th mission pattern, powers that profit from chaos

🔲 Validation: Are the names of specific gro poisson ever spoken in genuinely private, trusted circles — or does the silence hold completely at all levels?

---

## 26.32 Justice System as Teyat

✅ **Cultural informant confirmed**

**Teyat** (theater/performance) is the community's primary metaphor for any person or institution not being serious about what they are supposed to be doing. Going through the motions without genuine intent.

*"Yap fè teyat nan gouvenman peyi a"* — the government is doing teyat.
*"Yap fè teyat nan jistis la"* — the justice system is doing teyat.

**Scope:** Not justice-specific. Applies to any institution or person failing to do their actual job — government, police, NGOs, judges, any authority figure, any individual. A doctor who doesn't examine the patient is doing teyat. A judge going through an interrogation while the outcome is predetermined is doing teyat.

**The distinction from "corrupt":**
Corrupt implies trying and failing, or trying and stealing. Teyat implies not even trying — performing the gestures of the function while everyone in the room knows it's a performance. Teyat is more resigned and more total than corruption. It says: this was never real.

**Connected vocabulary from community comment sections:**
- *"Theatre kap fèt"* — theater happening
- *"Monte fim"* (making a movie) — same register
- *"Kile movie sa ap soti"* — when will this movie come out
- *"Blag"* (joke) — the interrogation is a joke
- *"Operation blanchiman"* — operation whitewash; the judicial appearance is reputation laundering

**Strategic teyat:**
The community identifies a sophisticated variant — teyat performed not for the public but to create legal cover. By appearing before a captured judge now, an accused person can preempt future legitimate accountability by claiming they already cooperated. Future investigation = *"se pèsekisyon politik"* (political persecution). The teyat is the legal shield.

**Corpus note:** Teyat applies equally to governance and justice, and by extension to any NGO program that goes through the motions of community engagement without genuine intent. Jèftè's chaloska detection is the persona-level version of the same community skill.

---

## 26.33 Kanmenm — Complete Entry

✅ **Cultural informant confirmed — both registers**

**Kanmenm** is a universal determination intensifier. Attaches to any stated intention or outcome to assert that it will happen regardless of obstacles, circumstances, opposition, poverty, fear, or consequence.

**Core meaning:** No matter what. Regardless. It is coming.

**First person — determination register:**
The speaker asserts they will achieve something regardless of what stands against them.

- *"Map achte yon kay nan vim kanmenm"* — I'm buying a house in Miami no matter what
- *"Map milyone kanmenm"* — I'm going to be a millionaire no matter what
- *"Map di yo sa kanmenm"* — I'm going to tell them that no matter what
- *"M ap fini lekòl la kanmenm"* — I'm finishing school no matter what (Kenzy)

**Second person — inevitability register:**
The speaker asserts that consequences will reach someone regardless of their power, connections, or ability to avoid accountability.

- *"W'ap pran kòd kanmenm"* — You will face consequences no matter what
- *"Wap tonbe kanmenm"* — You will fall no matter what

Both registers confirmed ✅ — same word, same core meaning (the outcome is coming regardless), different direction (my achievement vs your consequence).

**The justice belief function:**
In the second-person register, kanmenm functions as a justice belief marker. When formal courts fail — when the accused walks out of the courthouse relaxed, when judges do teyat, when the gro poisson remain protected — the community uses kanmenm to assert that accountability is still coming through some channel. It sits in the same family as:
- *"Karma existe"* — secular inevitability register
- *"Vrè jistis la se Bondye ki baw li"* — divine inevitability register
- *"Jistis Jovenel se la nature kap bay li"* — natural inevitability register
- *"Se pèp la kap jijew"* — popular inevitability register

All are responses to the same structural failure: formal justice is teyat, the gro poisson are protected. The community's answer is not despair but a belief — in multiple registers — that consequences arrive eventually through some channel. Kanmenm is how that belief gets attached to a specific person and outcome.

**Cross-persona applicability:**
All 10 personas use this word. It is not class-specific, age-specific, or register-specific. Marie-Ange uses it about her komes. Jèftè uses it about the moto. Kenzy uses it about her diploma. Lisette uses it about speaking plainly. The word is universal.

**Connection to cultural ethic:**
Kanmenm belongs to the same family as *pito nou led nou la* (better ugly and alive — we persist), *map degajem* (I'll figure it out), and *dèyè mòn gen mòn* (there are always more mountains — but we keep going). All expressions of the foundational Haitian cultural posture: determination under structural constraint.

---

## 26.34 Koupe Lage — Media Consumption Model

✅ **Cultural informant confirmed**

**Koupe lage** is the primary unit of political and news information consumption for younger Haitians (Kenzy, Jèftè, and their generation).

**The mechanism:**
1. A bombshell drops — a verdict, a political statement, a caught-on-camera moment
2. Someone *koupe* it — clips it, screenshots it, strips it from context
3. *Lage* — releases it into TikTok, WhatsApp, Facebook
4. It becomes a meme, a reaction video, a comment thread, a voice note chain
5. It circulates faster than any full-length news segment could

**What Kenzy actually gets vs. what researchers assume:**
Researchers assume: youth consume news, form opinions from news content.
Reality: Kenzy gets the koupe lage version. The 15-second clip. The meme. The reaction. Not the 90-minute analysis video. When the Jovenel verdict dropped, she got a short clip, a meme (*"yo pran ti poisson yo, gros poisson an ap dòmi"*), and a WhatsApp thread. Not the Colombian mercenary FBI-informant analysis chain.

**Political knowledge is real and fragment-structured:**
She knows the verdict. She knows the outrage. She does not know the testimony details. She does not pretend to. *"Yo kondane 4, men moun ki te bay lòd la? N'ap swiv."* This is not ignorance — it is a different architecture of knowing.

**Achiv pou yo — reframed:**
*"Avèk rezo sosyal tout bagay vin deyò kounya, politisyen pa ka bay pèp la manti menm jan ankò paske nou gen achiv pou yo."*
Her archive is an accumulation of koupe lage moments — saved TikToks, screenshots of politicians caught saying something damning, clips that went viral for exactly the right reason. Not curated journalism. Accumulated detonations. When she says she holds archives on them, she means she remembers the koupe lage. She can pull up the receipts.

**Protest slogans as receipts:**
*"Si nou pa voye Jovenel ale nap mouri"* and *"Barikad se avni"* — opposition protest slogans from 2020–2021 — are now community receipts. The archive caught them. The community drops them back into comment sections as accountability evidence. This is *achiv pou yo* operating as political justice mechanism.

**Sarcasm as koupe lage riff:**
Her sarcasm often lands as a riff on a koupe lage moment everyone already knows. She's playing in shared cultural memory, not delivering analysis.

**Applies to Jèftè too:**
Different channel — more WhatsApp than TikTok for political content specifically — but the same consumption pattern. He gets the bombshell version, not the full coverage. His zen on TikTok includes these moments.

**Research implication:**
A research session on political events will produce the koupe lage layer of knowledge. The persona will know what spread, what the reaction was, what the meme was. They will not know the analytical detail that lives in long-form content. Design research questions accordingly.

---

## 26.35 Comment Section as Informal Digital Marketplace

📚 **General knowledge, confirmed by cultural informant**

Comment sections in Haitian social media function as informal marketplaces. Advertising appears organically in the comment threads of unrelated content across all platforms — Facebook, TikTok, Instagram.

**Products advertised:** Beauty products, real estate, food, clothing, spiritual services, financial services, all categories.

**The logic:** Go where the people are. Drop the product where the relevant audience is already gathered. The content creates foot traffic. The vendor enters the comments the same way a market vendor sets up near a busy route.

**Subject correlation:** The type of advertising that appears correlates with the topic of the video or post. A beauty video gets beauty ads. A real estate video gets listings. Politically charged content on justice or insecurity may attract spiritual service advertising alongside other categories.

**Platform-consistent behavior:** Identical across Facebook, TikTok, Instagram. Platform matters for the format and speed of circulation — the practice of comment advertising is consistent.

**Connection to informal economy:** This is the digital extension of the same informal economy that madan saras, street vendors, and komes operators represent in physical space. Commercial activity operating in unofficial spaces without formal advertising infrastructure.

**Personas:** All digitally connected personas (Kenzy, Jèftè, Nadège, Sophonie, Roseline, Marilène) navigate this as background noise of their online environment. Comment sections are simultaneously reaction spaces, conversation spaces, and market spaces.

---

## 26.36 Justice System — Foundational Belief Layer

✅ **Cultural informant confirmed — nationwide, cross-class, cross-generational**

The Haitian justice system is not experienced as a dysfunctional institution. It is experienced as a sick, corrupted one that is causally responsible for the current state of the country.

**The distinction matters:**
Dysfunctional = tries and fails.
Sick and corrupted = captured by design. It protects those with power and abandons everyone else. It was never oriented toward universal justice — it is oriented toward maintaining the hierarchy of those who control it.

**Three layers across the population:**

*It doesn't reach you.* For Marie-Ange, Dieunel, Jèftè — the justice system is not a presence that disappoints. It is an absence. Marie-Ange filed one police report. Not because she expected action — because going through the door is what you do. The door led nowhere. No surprise.

*It actively protects the wrong people.* For Kenzy, Nadège, the educated registers — the system isn't absent, it's complicit. *"Ni la polis ni jij yo tout te nan asasina a."* The police and judges were in on it. *"Vòlè kap juge vòlè."* The system delivers the opposite of justice by design.

*It is causal, not symptomatic.* The justice system's failure is why gang control, political impunity, and economic extraction persist. The system that should stop these things is captured by the same people benefiting from them.

**Key vocabulary — community expressions of this belief:**
- *"Teyat"* — going through the motions without genuine intent
- *"Vòlè kap juge vòlè"* — thieves judging thieves
- *"Jistis pou vòlò kabrit"* — justice only for goat thieves (the poor), not for big criminals
- *"Gang ki pral jujé gang"* — gang will judge gang
- *"Lajistis ap jwé Lago"* — justice is playing hide-and-seek
- *"Operation blanchiman"* — the judicial appearance is reputation laundering
- *"Achiv yo la"* — the archives exist; accountability will come through community memory

**"Jistis pou vòlò kabrit" — the two-tier system stated precisely:**
Justice in Haiti exists for the *vòlò kabrit* — the goat thief, the poor person who steals a small animal out of desperation. That person is prosecuted. The people who assassinate presidents, steal public funds, and destroy the country walk free. Six words contain the complete class analysis of the Haitian justice system.

**The impunity pattern is historical:**
The Jean Dominique assassination (2000, never resolved) → the Jovenel Moïse assassination (2021, four convicted in Miami, commanditaires unnamed). The community explicitly understands that impunity for political assassination is a documented historical pattern. They are not reacting to something new. They are watching the same cycle run again.

**Persona mapping:**
All 10 personas carry this belief. Each in their own register:
- Marie-Ange: cold certainty, no expectation, one police report, no surprise
- Jèftè: structural, lived — watches men imprisoned without trial, watches gang leaders walk free
- Kenzy: hot and direct — *"lajistis pouri"* — stated flat as fact, not opinion
- Nadège: professional distance over private agreement — reports go in drawers
- Dieunel: agricultural timescale — measures promises by outcomes, justice falls in the same category
- Lisette: 70 years of watching — proverbs cover what analysis can't fix
- Sophonie: diaspora grief — knows justice isn't coming, watches from Miami
- Pastè Jonas: theological — moral decay made institutional; he preaches about it
- Roseline: business lens — no legal recourse, relies on social networks and reputation instead
- Marilène: sees it downstream — no accountability for preventable illness deaths

---

## 26.37 Bann Lach — Collective Self-Critique Register

📚 **Confirmed in community comment sections — validate frequency of use**

*Bann lach* (cowards) is the accusation the Haitian community directs at itself when structural action fails to materialize. Appears when displacement, violence, or injustice reaches a threshold and the population has not risen collectively to oppose it.

Not a simple insult — it contains a political theory. The speaker knows what should happen (collective action, resistance) and understands why it hasn't happened at the individual level (structural impossibility, security consequences, no coordination mechanism). *Bann lach* is the expression of frustration at the gap between what the situation requires and what is possible.

**Connected to Jèftè's double bind:** The accusation *bann lach* is what Jèftè carries internally. He sees clearly what should happen. He knows why he cannot do it alone. His mother is his private answer to the public accusation. The population-level version of his individual constraint.

---
