## 26.96 — Vèvè UNESCO Submission: Vodou Entering World Heritage

📚 **On March 26, 2026, Haitian authorities announced the submission of the
"Savoir-faire du Tracé-Vèvè d'Haïti"** to UNESCO for inscription on the
Representative List of Intangible Cultural Heritage of Humanity.

📚 **What are Vèvè:**
Vèvè are sacred geometric symbols traced on the ground during Vodou ceremonies
to invoke specific lwa (spirits). Each lwa has their own vèvè — a unique
spiritual diagram. Their origin is traced to the Arawak (indigenous Taíno)
drawings of the island's original inhabitants, making them a pre-colonial
cultural artifact absorbed and transformed through Vodou practice.

📚 **Haiti's UNESCO intangible heritage trajectory:**
| # | Element | Status |
|---|---|---|
| 1 | Soup Joumou | ✅ Recognized |
| 2 | Cassave | ✅ Recognized |
| 3 | Konpa/Compas | ✅ Recognized |
| 4 | Savoir-faire du Tracé-Vèvè | 🔲 Submitted March 26, 2026 |

📚 **Why this matters for the Jumo corpus:**
The Vèvè submission represents the Haitian state formally seeking global
recognition for a Vodou practice. Vodou was censored and persecuted for over
200 years — by early Haitian heads of state and by Catholic and Protestant
churches. It was only legally recognized as a formal religion in the 1980s.
The submission of Vèvè knowledge to UNESCO in 2026 represents a full arc:
from 200 years of state persecution to state-sponsored global recognition.

📚 **For the Vodou corpus layer already documented:**
The secrecy of Vodou practice (confirmed in the corpus — "completely secret,
wide practice and total secrecy coexist") operates alongside this public
institutional recognition. These are not contradictory. The practice remains
private; the knowledge is being formally inscribed in the public record.
These two registers — intimate secrecy and formal global heritage — coexist
in Haitian Vodou's position in 2026.

📚 **UNESCO also launched (March 2026):**
A project supporting "artistic creation, resumption of cultural events, and
access to cultural life in Haiti amid the security crisis" — call for applications
to cultural actors in Port-au-Prince. Culture as institutional response to crisis.

📚 **Haiti's UNESCO World Heritage Sites (existing):**
- **Parc National Historique** (inscribed 1982): Citadelle Laferrière,
  Sans-Souci Palace, Ramiers buildings — the first structures built by
  formerly enslaved people who conquered their freedom. These are buildings
  of universal symbolic significance.
- **Jacmel** (colonial city, on indicative list since 2004)

📚 **Culture as economic sector (UNESCO data):**
Artisans represent **10% of Haiti's active population** — approximately
400,000 people. The creative industries (crafts, books, music) are central
to Haiti's economic development. Culture is not soft infrastructure — it
is a primary employment sector.

---

## 26.97 — Haitian Food Culture: Diri ak Pwa and the National Plate

📚 **"Diri ak Pwa"** (also "Diri kole ak pwa") — Haiti's national dish.
Rice and beans, cooked together. **Ranked #2 globally among the 50 best
bean dishes** by Taste Atlas (November 2024). Among 50 options worldwide,
Haitian rice and beans placed second.

📚 **Historical root of the dish:**
Its origin traces to the period of slavery — rice and beans were among the
few foods distributed to enslaved people. The national dish literally emerged
from the conditions of captivity. It is sustenance that outlasted enslavement
and became identity.

📚 **Haitian saying about the dish:**
*"Un repas n'est complet que s'il contient du riz et des haricots."*
(A meal is only complete if it contains rice and beans.)

📚 **Varieties and accompaniments:**
- Beans: pinto, red, or black — regional variation
- Served plain or with sauce
- Common accompaniments: poulet créole (Creole chicken), vivaneau rouge
  (red snapper with tomatoes and onions), bouillon (goat or beef stew
  with potatoes and spices)
- Accessible across all social classes — ingredients simple and affordable

📚 **Nutritional framing:**
Rice provides starch, iron, proteins, B vitamins. Beans provide iron and
higher protein content. Together, a nutritionally complete meal. The dish
that fed enslaved people also nourishes free Haitians — it is both
history and daily sustenance.

📚 **Other confirmed Haitian dishes in public discourse:**

| Dish | Description | Notes |
|---|---|---|
| *Soup Joumou* | Pumpkin soup, Independence Day | UNESCO recognized |
| *Fritay* | Street fried food (pork, plantain, etc.) | Street food staple |
| *Griot* | Fried marinated pork | National favorite |
| *Lalo* | Jute leaf stew | Emblematic of northern Haiti, especially Artibonite |
| *Bouillie de riz* | Rice porridge | Common evening meal |
| *Tablet Kokoye* | Coconut confection | Traditional sweet |
| *Bouillon* | Goat/beef stew | Accompaniment to diri ak pwa |

📚 **Haitian products with international recognition:**
- **AYITIKA chocolate** — won award at Salon du Chocolat et de la Pâtisserie
  de Paris (Paris Chocolate and Pastry Show) for their **"Kanperen-80%"**
  single-origin dark chocolate tablet. Haitian cacao reaching global pastry
  markets.
- **Kola Choucoune** and **Ewo beer** — Haitian beverages reaching US and
  Canadian markets.

📚 **For Granmoun Lisette specifically:**
*Lalo* is described as "emblematic of northern Haiti, particularly popular
in Artibonite" — made with jute leaves. This is a regional dish with
Artibonite specificity that could be part of her household food vocabulary.
🔲 validate with Dulex.

---

## 26.98 — Haitian Culture at International Scale

📚 **"4 Kampé II"** — collaboration between **Joé Dwèt Filé** (franco-haïtien)
and **Burna Boy** (Nigeria) — ranked #10 on Billboard's chart of most-streamed
collaborations between Nigerian and French-speaking artists on Spotify. Haitian
music entering the global Afrobeats/Afropop circuit.

📚 **Francis Mercier** (Haitian DJ/producer) — released remix of "Magic In The
Air" with **Magic System** (Ivory Coast) and **Chawki** (Morocco). Pan-African
and Francophone music crossover.

📚 **Béchir Sylvain** — Haitian-American actor. Appeared in **"Jurassic World:
Rebirth"** world premiere at Lincoln Center, New York (June 2025). Wore a
creation by Haitian designer **Jovana Benoit**. Haitian fashion and film
reaching Hollywood-scale events simultaneously.

📚 **Fred Richard** — Haitian-American gymnast. **Triple NCAA all-around champion.**
Haitian excellence in sports beyond football documented.

📚 **CARIFESTA XV** (Caribbean Festival of Arts, Barbados, August 22–31, 2025):
- Haiti's theme: "Nos origines, nos réalisations, notre avenir"
- Led by **Erol Josué** — singer AND ethnologist, Director of the Faculty
  of Ethnology at Université d'État d'Haïti. A rare figure bridging academic
  ethnology and performing arts.
- Haiti presented: music, spirituality (Nanm Vodou group), Vodou dance troupes
  (21 Nanchon, Nègès Fla Vodou), workshops (Gout Dlo, Maison d'Escale)
- Culture presented as three dimensions: origins (Afro-Caribbean heritage),
  achievements (music, fashion, gastronomy), future (resilience)

📚 **"Les âmes bossales" documentary** (Director: François Perlier, released
February 4, 2026, after 7 years of filming):
- Characters: Charlotte, Foukifoura, Édris, Michou, Ramoncite
- Subjects: carnival, Vodou, street mobilizations, individual trajectories
- Carnaval de Jacmel: continues despite security climate — "la force du peuple"
- Director's frame: "La culture haïtienne populaire, forgée depuis la révolution
  des esclaves qui mena à l'indépendance en 1804, dégage un magnétisme hors du commun"
- Theme: "Résistance politique et artistique populaire, dans un pays au bord
  du chaos, où la rue est en feu mais où la dignité persiste"

📚 This documentary's framing — "the street is on fire but dignity persists" —
is the cultural articulation of what the corpus documents in structural terms
through personas. The artistic community is naming what Jumo is built to simulate.

## 26.102 — Haiti Cultural Exchange (HCX): Institutional Profile

📚 **Haiti Cultural Exchange (HCX)** is a New York City-based nonprofit organization.

📚 **Mission:** Develop, present, and promote the cultural expressions of the
Haitian people.

📚 **Founded:** 2009 by **seven Haitian women** — a founding act that is itself
culturally significant. The organization began as a deliberate intervention
against under-representation. Survey respondent quoted in their mission statement:
*"Haitian culture is the greatest story rarely told."*

📚 **Location:** 35 Lafayette Ave, Brooklyn, NY 11217.
Open Thursday–Sunday, 1–6pm; Wednesday by appointment.

📚 **Scale:**
- 450 artists and cultural figures presented per year
- Approximately 5,000 on-site audience members per year over the past decade
- Active on Facebook (@HaitiCulturalX), Twitter/X, Instagram, YouTube
  (HCXChannel), SoundCloud, and Spotify

📚 **The Brooklyn Haitian community it serves:**
The Haitian diaspora is the **7th largest immigrant group in New York City**,
with over **90,000 individuals residing in Brooklyn**. HCX's community surveyed
"often feels there is an exceeding lack of representation of Haitian arts and
culture" in New York City despite this population size.

📚 **Funders (FY26):** Ford Foundation, Howard Gilman Foundation, Jerome
Foundation, Mosaic Network and Fund, NYC Department of Cultural Affairs
(partnership with City Council), NY State Council on the Arts, NY State
Legislature, NY State Office of Children and Family Services, individual donors.

📚 **Political supporters:** NY State Assembly Member Rodneyse Bichotte Hermelyn;
NYC Council Speaker Adrienne Adams; NYC Council Members Crystal Hudson,
Rita Joseph, Farah Louis. Multiple Haitian-American elected officials in NYC
actively supporting a Haitian cultural institution reflects the political
representation dimension of diaspora cultural infrastructure.

---

## 26.103 — HCX Programs: Cultural Infrastructure in Practice

📚 **Arts Presentation programs:**

| Program | Description |
|---|---|
| **Diaspora NOW** | Contemporary diaspora arts presentation |
| **Haiti Film Fest** | Haitian cinema screening series |
| **Mizik Ayiti** | Haitian music performance series (First Thursdays format) |
| **Selebrasyon!** | Multidisciplinary festival format |

📚 **Artist Development programs:**

| Program | Kreyòl meaning | Focus |
|---|---|---|
| **Rasin Lakay** | Roots at Home | — |
| **Lakou Nou** | Our Yard/Compound | — |
| **HXNY** | Haiti Exchange New York | — |
| **Vizyon Atistik** | Artistic Vision | Artist development |

📚 **Cultural Engagement programs:**

| Program | Kreyòl meaning | Focus |
|---|---|---|
| **An n' Pale** | Let's Talk/Speak | Discussion/conversation |
| **Ti Atis** | Little Artist | Youth arts |

📚 **Recent featured work:**
- **Goussy Célestin's Ayiti Brass** performed at Mizik Ayiti First Thursdays
  (March 2024) — brass band bringing Haitian rhythmic tradition to NYC stages
- **"Lwa Pran M"** exhibition (2024) — title translates as "The lwa takes me /
  possesses me." A Vodou vocabulary word used openly as a contemporary
  exhibition title — showing how Vodou language operates without apology
  in diaspora artistic discourse, in contrast to the secrecy it requires in Haiti

---

## 26.104 — The Alan Lomax Archive Collaboration (April 2026)

📚 **Open call (April 29, 2026):** HCX issued an open call for visual artists
of Haitian descent to collaborate with the **Alan Lomax audio archive of Haiti
from the 1930s**.

📚 **Who was Alan Lomax:** An American ethnomusicologist and folklorist who
recorded music across the US, Caribbean, and elsewhere in the mid-20th century.
His 1930s Haiti recordings captured Vodou ceremonies, work songs, traditional
music — some of the earliest audio documentation of Haitian musical life.

📚 **What the collaboration represents:**
HCX is bridging a 1930s American-made archive of Haitian culture with
contemporary Haitian diaspora visual artists. This raises a productive tension
the corpus should note:

The archive was made by an outsider. The response is being made by insiders.
A foreign ethnomusicologist captured Haiti's sound in the 1930s — the same
decade the US occupied Haiti (1915–1934). The visual artists responding to
it in 2026 are Haitians reclaiming their own documented culture, reinterpreting
it through contemporary diaspora eyes, nearly 90 years later.

📚 **For the Jumo methodology:**
This collaboration is a micro-example of the larger dynamic the Jumo project
navigates: outside documentation vs. inside knowledge. Lomax archived what
he observed. Jumo is built on what Dulex knows from inside. The distinction
matters in both cases.

---

## 26.105 — Diaspora Cultural Infrastructure: What HCX Reveals

📚 **The founding by seven Haitian women** is a cultural fact about how diaspora
institutions are built. Not government programs, not NGO extensions — seven
individuals who identified a gap and created a permanent institution to fill it.
This mirrors the entrepreneurial survival logic documented in Marie-Ange's corpus
entry and in the broader informal economy layer.

📚 **The 90,000 Brooklyn Haitians / cultural invisibility gap:**
The community surveyed by HCX "often feels there is an exceeding lack of
representation of Haitian arts and culture" despite being the 7th largest
immigrant group in NYC. Scale of presence does not automatically produce
cultural visibility. The gap between demographic weight and cultural
representation is an active experience of the diaspora.

📚 **An n' Pale ("Let's Talk") as program title:**
The name of HCX's cultural engagement discussion program uses the exact
register — direct, communal, Kreyòl — that the Jumo trust architecture
documents as the only register that opens doors. A cultural institution
that names its conversation program in Kreyòl rather than in the language
of its funders is making a deliberate statement about who the program is for.

📚 **"Ti Atis" (youth arts) and "Lakou Nou" (our yard):**
These program names carry the lakou — the family compound as social organizing
principle — into a Brooklyn arts nonprofit context. The vocabulary of Haitian
communal life (the lakou as gathering space, as shared ground) adapts into
institutional programming language. Culture is not archived here — it is
actively transmitted.

📚 **Haiti Film Fest as diaspora infrastructure:**
A dedicated Haitian film festival in NYC means that Haitian cinema — including
documentary work like "July 7: Who Killed the President of Haiti?" (Robenson
Lauvince) and "Les âmes bossales" (François Perlier) — has a diaspora venue
for exhibition beyond mainstream distribution channels.

---

   as program branding, or is it too inside-community to translate?

   or is it primarily a diaspora/academic reference?

## CROSS-REFERENCE NOTE

📚 The HCX founding year (2009) coincides with the year after the global
financial crisis and one year before the 2010 earthquake. The institution
was built during one of the most difficult periods for Haiti and the diaspora.
Its survival and growth through the 2010 earthquake, the Jovenel assassination,
the current security crisis, and the TPS/immigration uncertainty confirms what
the corpus documents about Haitian community resilience: institutions built
for long-term presence, not crisis response.

📚 The political supporter list (Rodneyse Bichotte Hermelyn, Adrienne Adams,
Crystal Hudson, Rita Joseph, Farah Louis) documents something the corpus
does not yet have: **Haitian-Americans in elected political positions in the US.**
This is Sophonie's political landscape — not just immigrant community member,
but community with elected representation. This matters for how she frames
her dual identity and civic engagement.

## 26.107 — RTVC: Institutional Profile

📚 **Radio Télévision Caraïbes (RTVC)** — one of Haiti's primary broadcast
media institutions. French-language primary; also produces content in Kreyòl.
Frequency: **94.5 FM** (Port-au-Prince). Live TV streaming at
radiotelecaraibes.com. Social: @rtvchaiti (Facebook, X, Instagram, YouTube).

📚 **Stated mission:** "Your trusted source for news, entertainment, and
information in Haiti... an essential platform for informing, engaging, and
actively participating in Haitian public life."

📚 **Named programs:**

| Program | Format | Language |
|---|---|---|
| **Matin Caraïbes** | Morning show | French |
| **Café Philo** | Philosophical discussion | French |
| **Caraïbes Culture+** | Culture | French |
| **Vitrine** | Showcase | French |
| **Playlist** | Music | French |
| **Studiofest** | Studio performances | French |
| **TekTek** | Technology (host: John Boisguéné) | French/Kreyòl |
| **22 Live** | Live news/events | French/Kreyòl |
| **Bilten Enfomasyon** | Kreyòl news bulletin | **Kreyòl** |

📚 **The Bilten Enfomasyon is structurally important.** RTVC produces a dedicated
Kreyòl-language news bulletin — confirmed presenter: Mary Stéphanie Laguerre;
realization: Ralph Deronvil. This is the daily news for Haitians without French
literacy. For Granmoun Lisette and Dieunel (rural, oral-only), a Kreyòl news
bulletin on a major station is a realistic information access point via radio.

📚 **RTVC as Nadège's media world:** RTVC's Café Philo and Caraïbes Culture+ —
analytical, philosophical programming in French — map directly to the media
environment of Haiti's educated professional class. This is likely a reference
station for Nadège.

---

## 26.108 — RTVC Political Coverage: Key Stories (2025–2026)

📚 **IDA party debate on elections (December 27, 2025):**
The Inisyativ pou Devlope Ayiti (IDA, founded 2022) held a public debate at
Hôtel Oasis, Port-au-Prince. Core positions:
- No elections without prior security improvement — "security is a prerequisite
  for any electoral consultation"
- Without broad internal political consensus, "international partners will
  continue to decisively influence the national agenda"
- Repeated transitions are themselves an aggravating factor for instability
- Youth political education named as key to rebuilding credible political organizations
- Former senator Pierre Francky Exius: a conditional national agreement must
  come before elections, recentered on security

📚 **This adds texture to the existing elections corpus layer.** The IDA debate
articulates in public what the corpus already documents as a structural reality:
security first, elections second — and without internal consensus, Haiti's
political future is determined externally. Kenzy's "vòlè kap juge vòlè" register
is the community version of this same analysis.

📚 **Montana accord signatories and CPT transition:**
Montana accord signataires attempting to reach the next CPT president, with
Fritz Alphonse Jean named as a possible next CPT president. This is current
transition politics (May 2026).

📚 **US warship in Port-au-Prince bay (February 3, 2026):**
An American military vessel arrived in the bay of Port-au-Prince on the evening
of Tuesday, February 3, 2026. Coverage was factual, no further context
in available snippets. New event — not previously in corpus. 🔲 Significance
and community reception need validation.

📚 **US Embassy delivering rolling equipment to PNH:**
"PNH : Anbasad Amerikèn Remèt yon Lo Materyèl Woulan ak Lapolis Nasyonal" —
The US Embassy delivered operational/rolling equipment to Haiti's National Police.
External material support to PNH documented in Kreyòl RTVC coverage.

---

## 26.109 — RTVC Health Coverage: New Hospital Openings

📚 **This directly updates the health corpus (Section 26.75).**

📚 **CAMEDYC hospital at Delmas 60 (March 28, 2026):**
CAMEDYC inaugurated a new hospital at 8, Delmas 60, Port-au-Prince. The
initiative aims to "significantly strengthen healthcare provision in the
metropolitan region" in a context where "access to care remains limited for
a significant part of the population."

📚 **OPTIMUM hospital at Delmas 39:**
Opened approximately one year ago (referenced in RTVC's "22 Live" content).
Grand opening at Delmas 39, Port-au-Prince.

📚 **Critical context from the health corpus:** While MSF was permanently
closing Turgeau (October 2025) and approximately 30 hospitals had ceased
operations, private hospital openings at Delmas 60 and Delmas 39 confirm
that healthcare infrastructure is not uniformly collapsing — it is bifurcating.
Private facilities are opening in areas accessible to those who can pay.
Public and NGO emergency care serving working-class and poor populations
is closing. The two trends are simultaneous and represent a class divergence
in healthcare access.

📚 **For Marilène:** Private hospitals at Delmas are not her referral pathway.
Her patients — peri-urban working-class — cannot access private care. The
health system bifurcation is the structural context of her daily navigation.

---

## 26.110 — RTVC Technology Coverage: TekTek and Haiti's AI Moment

📚 **TekTek** is RTVC's dedicated technology program, hosted by **John Boisguéné**.
Topics confirmed from available content:
- TikTok US crackdown ("Pourquoi TikTok est-il dans le viseur des États-Unis?")
- Starlink in Haiti ("Kisa teknoloji Starlink lan ye vreman?")
- Social media as danger for Haitian youth ("Réseaux Sociaux yon malè pandye
  sou lavi chak grenn Ayisyen" — Social media, a danger hanging over every
  Haitian's life)
- E-commerce basics
- Computer networking fundamentals in Kreyòl
- Microsoft Excel tutorials in Kreyòl
- AI and technology weekly news (TekTalk format)

📚 **For Kenzy:** TikTok being covered on RTVC as a political/legal story means
Kenzy's primary platform is in his broader media environment — not just as a
consumption tool but as a subject of public debate. The title "Social media,
a danger hanging over every Haitian's life" is the older-generation institutional
framing of what Kenzy lives inside.

📚 **BANJ ProAI program — Haiti enters AI discourse (March 2026):**
BANJ (an institution — likely BANJ incubator/innovation hub) launched **ProAI**,
a program to train professionals in AI and adapt it to Haitian realities.
RTVC covered this as a news story, framing it as significant.

📚 **Potential AI applications proposed for Haiti:**
- Agricultural data management
- Natural disaster risk anticipation
- Economic trend analysis
- Education and health planning

📚 **Key question raised in RTVC coverage:**
"Does Haiti have a real national AI strategy?" RTVC framed ProAI as promising
but noted its actual impact depends on producing concrete results: local tech
projects, scientific collaborations, Haiti-adapted innovations.

📚 **For Jumo specifically:**
An AI program (ProAI) launching in Haiti, covered on national media (RTVC), in
the same month as the Jumo corpus is being built, confirms that AI as a tool
for Haiti's development is entering public institutional discourse. Jumo is not
arriving in a vacuum — it is entering a moment when Haiti's own institutions
are beginning to ask what AI can do for them.

---

## 26.111 — Café Philo: Bois Caïman and the National Calendar

📚 **Café Philo** dedicated a segment to: "L'Invisibilisation de Bois Caïman
dans le calendrier national: (re)penser le temps symbolique de la République
d'Haïti."

📚 **What Bois Caïman is:**
The ceremony held the night of **August 14, 1791** in the forests near
Cap-Haïtien — widely considered the spiritual and organizational launching
point of the Haitian Revolution. Led by Boukman Dutty and Cécile Fatiman,
it was a Vodou ceremony that preceded the August 22, 1791 uprising.
It is the moment where the enslaved people of Saint-Domingue made their
collective pact for freedom, invoking the lwa. It is the Vodou origin of
Haitian independence.

📚 **The invisibilization debate:**
Despite being the spiritual spark of independence, Bois Caïman does not
appear prominently in Haiti's official national commemorative calendar.
The Café Philo segment invites rethinking Haiti's "symbolic time" — what
the republic officially remembers and marks, and what it leaves in shadow.

📚 **Why this matters for the Jumo corpus:**
The Vodou origin of Haitian independence (Bois Caïman) is in structural
tension with the country's Catholic surface identity and with Evangelical
rejection of Vodou entirely. The debate about whether Bois Caïman belongs
in the national calendar is:
- A Vodou recognition debate
- A colonial/post-colonial memory debate
- A question about who the Haitian state officially honors

📚 **For Pastè Jonas:** An evangelical pastor who likes football and preaches
against gambling would almost certainly have a position on whether Bois Caïman
belongs in the national calendar. His answer is a significant persona detail.
🔲 Validation needed.

📚 **For Granmoun Lisette:** As the elder persona closest to rasin (roots) and
Vodou practice, her relationship to Bois Caïman — as history, as ceremony, as
living memory — may be completely different from how it is discussed in a
Port-au-Prince philosophical program. 🔲 Validation needed.

---

## 26.112 — Ayiti VodouFest: Vodou as Public Cultural Event

📚 **"Première édition de 'Ayiti VodouFest'"** — described by RTVC as
"un coup d'essai, un coup de maître" (a first attempt, a masterpiece). A
dedicated Vodou festival in Haiti. Year not specified in available snippets
but referenced in RTVC's cultural programming.

📚 **Significance:** The existence of a named, organized VodouFest — alongside
the Vèvè UNESCO submission and the "Lwa Pran M" exhibition title already in
the corpus — confirms a trajectory: Vodou is moving from purely private practice
toward organized public cultural presentation, even inside Haiti.

📚 **This does not contradict the secrecy documented in the corpus.**
The corpus documents that individual Vodou consultation is completely secret.
What is emerging publicly is cultural Vodou — performance, festival, artistic
expression, UNESCO heritage application. Private practice remains invisible;
cultural Vodou is becoming visible. Both registers are simultaneously true.

📚 **For Pastè Jonas:** A VodouFest in Haiti would be exactly the kind of
cultural event he would feel compelled to address from the pulpit. His register —
does he condemn it, navigate it pastorally, or address it as a cultural vs.
spiritual distinction? 🔲 Needs validation.

---

## 26.113 — "52 Ans Plus Tard": The World Cup Frame

📚 RTVC's World Cup headline: **"52 ans plus tard, Haïti s'offre un billet
pour la Coupe du monde 2026"** — 52 years later, Haiti gets a World Cup ticket.

📚 **Haiti's last World Cup was 1974** — the Munich World Cup. This is the frame
through which RTVC and by extension Haitian media presents the 2026 qualification:
not just a sports achievement but a 52-year gap being closed. A generation that
never saw Haiti at a World Cup finally will.

📚 **For Kenzy:** He is 21 years old. He was born 31 years after Haiti's last
World Cup. "52 years later" is not nostalgia for him — it is the first time
in his lifetime. The emotional register of this is entirely different from
older Haitians who remember 1974. 🔲 How Kenzy frames the 52-year gap —
history he knows vs. lived experience — needs validation.

📚 **For Granmoun Lisette:** She was alive in 1974. The 52-year frame may
carry a specific generational weight for her. 🔲 Validate.

---

## 26.115 — Métronome FM: Institutional Profile

📚 **Métronome FM** — "la radio, la vraie" (the radio, the real one). Tagline
positions it as credible, serious journalism against a media landscape it implies
lacks authenticity. French-language, editorial/analytical focus.

📚 **Categories:** Société (Society), National, Sport, Économie, Éditorial.
Social: @metronomehaiti (Facebook), @Radio_Metronome (Twitter/X). Live streaming
available at metronomehaiti.com/ecoutez-radio-metronome/.

📚 **Primary editorial voice: Jean Corvington.** His register is intellectual
French political analysis — citing Hannah Arendt, using constitutional vocabulary,
framing Haiti's crisis through political philosophy. This is the educated class's
analytical language. Nadège would read or listen to content like this. Kenzy
would encounter it as koupe lage fragments — a phrase, a headline, a clip.

---

## 26.116 — Editorial Analysis: The CPT Transition as Illegitimate Power

📚 **"Haïti: la transition qui ne doit rien à personne" (March 11, 2026)**
By Jean Corvington. Key analytical positions:

📚 The opening thesis: *"A transitional power that owes its existence to no one
always ends up no longer feeling accountable to anything, except the perpetuation
of its own privileges."*

📚 The precise institutional critique: *"In Haiti, we are no longer talking about
a simple governance failure, but an assumed drift: an executive without popular
mandate, without electoral legitimacy, but with an astonishing expertise for
organizing its own impunity."*

📚 The framing: *"Le pouvoir sans peuple: une légitimité en carton"* —
Power without the people: cardboard legitimacy.

📚 Hannah Arendt invoked: *"Power is born where people act together, and
disappears when this link breaks. Here, the link is broken, but the power
remains — like a ghost clinging to the walls of a hollowed-out state."*

📚 The mechanism described: *"no people consulted, no program debated, no
ballot boxes — only signatures between political, diplomatic, and economic actors."*

📚 **For the corpus:** This editorial articulates in intellectual French what
the Jumo corpus already documents in community Kreyòl. The "ghost clinging to
the walls of a hollowed-out state" maps precisely onto *teyat* — going through
the motions. *Légitimité en carton* maps onto Kenzy's *vòlè kap juge vòlè.*
The educated class and the street arrive at the same analysis in different registers.

---

## 26.117 — Editorial Analysis: The Pacte National as Constitutional Power Grab

📚 **"Un pouvoir d'exception qui s'arroge le droit de changer les règles"
(March 18, 2026)** By Jean Corvington. Subject: the "Pacte national pour
la stabilité et les élections" — a political pact between transition actors.

📚 **The Pacte's stated purpose:** Present itself as a crisis exit document,
a path toward elections and stability.

📚 **What Métronome's analysis reveals in Articles 12–15 and 24:**
The Pacte constitutes "a dangerous attempt to capture constituent power,
blur electoral rules, and extend the transition indefinitely without real
accountability."

📚 **Article 13 specifically:** Changes to constitutional arrangements will be
determined "in consultation" between the current power and the "forces vives" —
political actors, signatories or not. The analysis: *"behind the consensual
vocabulary, it is not the sovereign people who set the boundaries of change,
but a circle [of insiders]."*

📚 **The mechanism:** Under cover of "une période d'exception" (an exceptional
period), a silent slide — *glissement silencieux* — whereby a transitional
government without popular legitimacy attributes itself the right to make major
constitutional modifications.

📚 **New vocabulary confirmed from Métronome editorials:**

| Term | Meaning | Register |
|---|---|---|
| *Légitimité en carton* | Cardboard legitimacy | Editorial/intellectual |
| *Expertise pour organiser sa propre impunité* | Expertise for organizing its own impunity | Editorial/intellectual |
| *Glissement silencieux* | Silent slide (of power) | Editorial/intellectual |
| *Pouvoir constituant capté* | Constituent power captured | Constitutional analysis |
| *Période d'exception* | Exceptional period — the transition's self-justification | Official/contested |
| *Forces vives* | Living forces — political actors outside government | Political vocabulary |
| *Reddition de comptes* | Accountability — what the transition avoids | Standard French |
| *Un État vidé* | A hollowed-out state | Editorial/intellectual |

📚 **Cross-reference with existing corpus:**
Métronome's *légitimité en carton* (intellectual French register) =
community Kreyòl *teyat* (going through motions without genuine intent).
Métronome's *expertise pour organiser sa propre impunité* (educated analysis) =
community Kreyòl *vòlè kap juge vòlè* (thieves judging thieves).
These are the same institutional reality described from two class positions.
Both belong in the corpus because both appear in how different personas process
the same political reality.

---

## 26.118 — The "Peuple Haïtien" Question as Editorial Frame

📚 Métronome's headline: **"Et le Peuple Haïtien dans tout ça?"** —
And the Haitian People in all this?

📚 This framing — where is the Haitian people in all these political
negotiations between elites, international actors, and transitional power? —
is the central question the corpus also asks, from the community side, through
every persona. The Métronome editorial register and the community Kreyòl
register are asking the same question from opposite ends of the social spectrum.

---

## 26.119 — ONASAPS: Social Protection as National Emergency

📚 **ONASAPS** (Office National d'Assistance Sociale et de Protection Sociale) —
Haiti's national social assistance and social protection institution.
Métronome headline: **"L'ONASAPS: Une Urgence Nationale Toujours en Attente"**
— A National Emergency Still Waiting.

📚 **What ONASAPS represents for the corpus:**
This is the state institution that should provide a social safety net for
Marie-Ange, Granmoun Lisette, and Jèftè. The fact that it is described as a
"national emergency still waiting" — not yet functional at the level of need —
confirms the structural gap between institutional existence and operational reality.

📚 **Marie-Ange has no social protection.** Her hypertension goes untreated
because she cannot lose a day of komes. If ONASAPS functioned at scale, that
equation would change. It does not function at scale. The corpus documents the
lived consequence; Métronome names the institutional failure.

---

## 26.120 — SOS/Grand-Gosier: Justice Gap at the Local Level

📚 Métronome headline: **"SOS/Grand-Gosier: Pas de juge de Paix, pas de tribunal,
la population aux abois"** — No justice of the peace, no tribunal, the population
in despair.

📚 **Grand-Gosier** is a commune in the Sud-Est department of Haiti. The
community has no functioning local judicial presence — no justice of the peace,
no tribunal.

📚 **What this adds to the justice corpus layer:**
The corpus already documents *jistis pou vòlò kabrit* (justice only for goat
thieves), *vòlè kap juge vòlè* (thieves judging thieves), and the justice
system as captured. The Grand-Gosier story adds a different dimension: not
captured justice, but absent justice. In some communities, the judicial
infrastructure doesn't exist at all at the local level — not corrupt, simply
not present. The population is "aux abois" — at their wits' end — not because
the court fails them but because there is no court.

📚 **For Granmoun Lisette:** Rural Artibonite. If Grand-Gosier in Sud-Est has
no local judicial presence, similar gaps likely exist in rural Artibonite.
The Vodou-as-justice pathway (already confirmed in the corpus) is the
community's response to exactly this kind of institutional absence. 🔲 validate.

📚 **Jovenel assassination — lawyers arrested in Badio's hiding place:**
The investigation continues. Three lawyers were arrested in the hiding place
of "Badio" — likely referring to one of the named suspects. The assassination
case is generating ongoing arrests. This is the current judicial moment the
corpus already documents around the May 8, 2026 verdict.

The consortium organizing the "Conférence Nationale" (a proposed national
dialogue process) submitted its report in May 2025. As of early 2026, the
conference has apparently not materialized into action. The report exists;
the action doesn't follow. Standard Haitian institutional pattern.

📚 **Security sector reform analysis:**
Métronome published a formal analysis of security sector reform in Haiti,
framing it as "between major issues and urgent necessity." The existence of
this analysis in media confirms the security sector reform debate is in
public discourse — not just in NGO reports.

📚 **$6 million for northern farmers:**
Métronome covered a workshop at Cap-Haïtien bringing together agriculture
and environment ministry officials, agricultural sector representatives, and
others around a $6 million package to improve farmers' conditions in the
Grand Nord (northern Haiti). Regional agriculture investment documented.

📚 **The Messi/PSG/Inter Miami effect — confirmed via Haitian media:**
Métronome covered Messi's move to Inter Miami as a news story — including
the PSG subscriber loss (2M Instagram followers) and Inter Miami subscriber
gain (3M). The player loyalty mechanism documented in Correction #039 is
confirmed as a story that Haitian sports media actively followed. For Haitians
who followed Messi to PSG, the move to Inter Miami brings him to Sophonie's
geographic zone. 🔲 Does Sophonie attend Inter Miami matches?

📚 **Franck Mivenstherley Joseph (age 13) — CF Montréal Metro CUP 2026:**
A 13-year-old Haitian footballer selected for the Metro CUP 2026 with
CF Montréal's development program (May 14, 2026). The Haitian football
pipeline now extends to youth academies in Canada — not just European
clubs. The next generation of World Cup players is being developed in
North American academies alongside European ones.

📚 **"Le refus de l'eurocentrisme en Afrique, à quand une réplique haïtienne?"**
— Refusing Eurocentrism in Africa: when will Haiti have its equivalent?
This headline shows Métronome engaging with pan-African political thought
and asking whether Haiti will join the movement away from European frameworks.
For the corpus — this is the intellectual class's engagement with decolonial
discourse. It maps onto the Bois Caïman debate (Section 26.111) and onto
the deeper question of whether Haiti's independence revolution is properly
honored in its own national consciousness.

## 26.123 — Chaloska: Complete Cultural History

✅ **Source: Dulex (cultural informant) | Session 4, May 2026**

**Historical origin:**
Charles Oscar Étienne — a Haitian military chief who killed more than 150 political
prisoners in Port-au-Prince during the American occupation of Haiti in 1915. After
his death, the Haitian people transformed him into a carnival *bougeyman* — a figure
of fear and collective mockery in carnival bands.

**Appearance:**
People who wear the Chaloska costume dress in military clothing (the uniform of
institutional power) and wear a mask with a large red mouth and long teeth —
*mechanste ak awogans* (wickedness and arrogance) made visible. The costume holds
the political argument: the official exterior concealing the monstrous face underneath.

**Carnival performance — especially in Jacmel:**
During carnival, Chaloska characters play scenes where they deliberately die and are
replaced by each other in the same costume. One falls. Another rises. The system
repeats. The point is not the individual occupying the role — it is the role, the
position, the pattern that reproduces itself regardless of who is inside the costume.
This is a way for the people to express their frustration with bad governance through
collective, public performance.

**Colonial layer:**
The character originates from a Haitian who wielded power against Haitians under
American occupation. Institutional costume, wrong system. When Haitians use this word
today, that colonial collaboration layer is embedded in it — however submerged.

**When used as a term for a person or institution:**
To call something *Chaloska* is to place it inside the carnival parade — costumed in
official legitimacy, face grotesque underneath, performing a role that has been
performed before and will be performed again after this one falls. It is simultaneously:
- A historical reference (1915, colonial collaboration)
- A political analysis (the system repeats)
- A collective act (the crowd recognizes the costume)
- A mockery (the carnival register)
- A warning (the teeth in the mask)

**NOT simply "imposter."** That translation loses everything.

**Vocabulary correction (#053):**
"Farouche" in Haitian Kreyòl means: to mock, make fun of, laugh at someone. NOT the
French meaning (wild, fierce, unsociable). This error class — French cognate assumed
into Kreyòl — must not be repeated. Any Kreyòl word that resembles a French word
requires explicit validation before use.

**Confirmed usage across personas:**
- Nadège (to Haitian colleagues about her NGO's programs): *"Chaloska. Nou konnen istwa sa a."*
  The program dies. Another rises in the same costume. System repeats.
- Pastè Jonas (from pulpit, without naming the organization): congregation sees the
  military uniform, the grotesque mask. He does not need to name names.
- Roseline (privately about loan officers): brochure = military uniform. Hidden fees +
  disappearing officer = the mask. They are replaced. Same costume. Same pattern.

---

## 26.124 — Vodou Disclosure Architecture: Secrecy and Coded Healthcare Language

✅ **Source: Dulex (cultural informant) | Session 4, May 2026**

**Core principle:**
Vodou practice is common but secret. It is not disclosed to outsiders. Only people in
a small inner circle know what is really going on — whether a houngan was consulted
or not. This confidentiality is structural — built over centuries of external pressure
(Catholic condemnation, missionary campaigns, government persecution, international
scrutiny). Secrecy is not shame. It is protection.

**The inner circle:**
Even within a community, even among neighbors, the knowledge of whether a houngan
was consulted stays inside the family's inner ring. People outside the circle —
researchers, NGO workers, health staff, international colleagues — are not inside it.
None of them are told directly.

**Healthcare disclosure pattern:**
A family might disclose some of it *loosely* to a nurse or health worker — never
directly, never completely. They give indirect signals, not direct disclosure. They
do not say: "We consulted the houngan." They say things that signal that reality
without naming it.

**The five coded phrases (✅ validated):**

1. *"Sanble sa pa maladi doktè"*
   — Seems like this is not a doctor's illness.
   The family has already made a diagnostic assessment: this illness category does not
   belong to the medical domain. They are not rejecting the doctor — they are placing
   the illness in a different category.

2. *"Nou pa konprann li ditou"*
   — We don't understand it at all.
   Incomprehensibility of the illness to the clinical system is itself the evidence.
   If the doctor could explain it, it would be a doctor's illness.

3. *"Tout remèd doktè bay pa fè anyen"*
   — All the medicine the doctor gives does nothing.
   Treatment failure as primary evidence of spiritual etiology.

4. *"Lè li lakay la li gen tout problem"*
   — When he is at home, he has all kinds of problems.
   Spatial manifestation pattern — the illness presents in relation to a specific
   location or domestic space. Meaningful within Vodou diagnostic frameworks.

5. *"Doktè fè radyografi yo — yo pa janm wè kòz maladi a"*
   — The doctors did X-rays — they never found the cause of the illness.
   Clinical technology failure as confirmation of non-clinical etiology. The most
   powerful signal: the formal diagnostic system looked and could not find it.

**For researchers and health program designers:**
These five phrases are the maximum disclosure available to outsiders. Asking directly
whether a houngan was consulted produces denial — not deception, but boundary
maintenance. The coded language is real information. The full consultation details
stay in the circle. The result of the consultation may travel outward through the
proxy system. The specifics do not.

---

## 26.125 — Sòl: Informal Rotating Savings — Mechanics, Trust Architecture, Legal Void

✅ **Source: Dulex (cultural informant) | Session 4, May 2026**

**What it is:**
A rotating savings club. Members contribute a fixed amount regularly. Each rotation,
one member receives the full pot. The rotation continues until every member has
received once.

**Entry mechanism:**
You cannot join a sòl by applying. You join because someone already inside the group
trusts you enough to put their own standing behind you. The voucher takes on implicit
accountability for the person they introduce. If you default, they are accountable
to the group.

Entry is restricted to: close friends, people you know personally, or someone vouched
for by a trusted existing member. Anonymous participation does not exist.

**The risk:**
The person who receives the pot can take it and disappear. No legal recourse exists.
No law regulates the sòl. The only consequences are social — community reputation
damage, family pressure, exclusion from future groups — which require community
presence to apply. Someone who leaves the area after taking the pot faces no
consequence at all.

**Legal status:**
Entirely outside the formal financial system. No registration, no documentation,
no institutional oversight, no legal protection for participants.

**Why it functions anyway:**
The trust architecture IS the regulatory framework. There is no other one. The system
functions because the entry filter is strict enough to make default rare. It does not
function when that filter is bypassed.

**For microfinance product designers:**
The sòl is not an inferior version of formal savings. It is a parallel system built
on trust architecture rather than institutional architecture. Formal financial products
sit alongside it, not above it. Products that treat it as a gap to be filled will be
rejected in favor of it. Understanding its mechanics is prerequisite to designing
products that coexist with it.

**Confirmed sòl participation across personas:**
- Marie-Ange: active, market women network, cannot miss payment without losing standing
- Roseline: active, with people she knows personally (boutique peers, close friends),
  not church-affiliated (church group correction — see #059)
- Marilène: active, with peer health workers

---

## 26.126 — Cap-Haïtien (Okap): Dialect, Civic Identity, Displacement Surge

✅ **Source: Dulex (cultural informant) | Session 4, May 2026**

**Name:**
People from Cap-Haïtien call their city *Okap*. Not Cap-Haïtien. Not Le Cap. *Okap*.
This is the correct local usage. Using "Cap-Haïtien" marks an outsider.

**Okap Kreyòl dialect:**
Okap people do not speak Kreyòl the same way as Port-au-Prince people. The difference
is clear and audible immediately.

PaP (Port-au-Prince) forms:
- *machin sa se pam* — this car is mine
- *sa se machin mwen* — this is my car

Okap forms:
- *machin sa se kinanm* — this car is mine (contracted from *ki nan mwen*)
- *sa se machin anm* — this is my car (contracted from *a mwen*)

*Kinanm* and *anm* are the Okap possessive forms — fused contractions specific to
northern Kreyòl. These are dialect markers, not accent variations.

Port-au-Prince people sometimes *farouche* (mock, make fun of) how Okap people speak.
*"Moun Pòtoprens toujou panse yo pi eklere e pi entelijan ke moun ki soti nan rès
peyi a."* — Port-au-Prince people always think they are more educated and more
intelligent than people from the rest of the country. Capois people have verified this
enough times to say *toujou* (always).

**Civic identity:**
✅ Validated voice sample (Roseline Augustin, Session 4):
*"Vil la chaje nouvo je, ou pa konnen kiyes ki bon ak move moun, men tout moun ap veye
paske nou pap janm kite Okap rive nan nivo Pòtoprens ye a. Nou pap kite bandi vin mete
nou deyò menm jan epi pran vil nan man nou. Yap pran kale paske moun Okap pa nan rans
ak bandi."*

Translation: "The city is full of new eyes — you don't know who are good and bad
people. But everyone is watching, because we will never let Okap reach the level
Port-au-Prince is at. We won't let bandits push us out the same way and take the city
out of our hands. They'll get beaten, because Okap people don't play around with
bandits."

*Moun Okap pa nan rans ak bandi.* — This is civic identity, not just a position.

**Displacement surge:**
✅ Validated voice sample (Roseline Augustin, Session 4):
*"Depi kèk tan moun anvayi nou nan vil la, Okap se yon ti pla men, pa gen kote pou
tout moun sa yo. Bandi Pòtoprens mete tout moun deyò, tout moun kouri ak pakèt nan
men, se okap yo vini. Boutik la vann plis kounya paske zone nan vin gen plis moun men,
sa vin fè pri tout bagay monte tou paske vin gen plis demand. Kay vin pi chè, blòk ak
siman vin pi chè, vil la menm vin 'sal kou peny ti dan', pi mal pase jan l te ye avan."*

*Sal kou peny ti dan* — dirty like a fine-toothed comb: a city overcrowded to
filth, every gap filled, accumulated grime between every tooth.

**Two-register system (Cap-Haïtien):**
Public/commercial: "the situation," "things have changed," "the city is under pressure."
Private/trusted: *moun anvayi nou* (people invaded us), *bandi* (bandits), *pakèt nan
men* (bag in hand). The public version is not dishonest — it is contextually managed.
The private version is what she carries.

**DR-Haiti — northern border:**
Cap-Haïtien is in the north. The Ouanaminthe-Dajabón crossing is the primary northern
border point. Commercial merchants from Okap cross regularly to buy inventory in the
Dominican Republic (*Sendomeng*). This is standard practice for capois boutique owners.

✅ Validated voice sample — DR border (Roseline Augustin, Session 4):
*"Dominiken yo se vòlè yo ye, yo fè ayisyen anpil abi men malerezman nou pa gen leta
pou pale pou nou. Yon viza dominiken konn koute 50 dola epi raketè fè nou peye l jiska
400 dola, pafwa ou pa menm ka jwenn li. Pafwa lè w ap travèse fwontyè a, yo vòlè kòb
ou. Ayisyen k'ap viv Sendomeng yo menm se pa de mizè y ap pase. Dominiken konn kenbe
yo, depòte yo malgre papye yo bon, apre sa lè pou Ayisyen sa yo retounen DR ankò se
yon lòt kòb yo oblije peye, bagay vòlè net."*

Key phrase: *"malerezman nou pa gen leta pou pale pou nou"* — unfortunately we have
no state to speak for us. The absent state as structural condition enabling the abuse.
See also Section 26.133 (cross-persona structural themes).

---

## 26.127 — Religious Calendars: Global Institutional Framework

✅ **Source: Dulex (cultural informant) | Session 4, May 2026**

**Core principle:**
All major religious denominations in Haiti follow their own global institutional
calendars — not Haitian-specific ones.

- Catholics follow the global Catholic calendar
- Seventh-day Adventists (SDA) follow the global Adventist calendar
- Jehovah's Witnesses follow the global JW schedule

The calendar itself is not Haitian-specific for any of these denominations.

**What IS Haitian-specific:**
The cultural expression around those calendars — the food, the gatherings, the social
rituals, the way holidays are lived in community. This expression varies by
denomination, region, family, and individual practice.

**Implication for corpus and persona system:**
- Do not describe a holiday calendar as *Haitian*. Describe Haitian *expression* around
  a global calendar.
- SDA and JW in Haiti practice the same calendar and doctrine as SDA and JW worldwide.
  They are not shaped by Haitian cultural specificity in their religious practice.
- Do not apply Haitian Catholic or Vodou-layer assumptions to SDA or JW households.
- The two-layer system (Catholic surface + Vodou parallel) described in Section 2.1
  applies to Catholic and mainstream Protestant households — NOT to SDA or JW households.

**Jehovah's Witnesses:**
Do not celebrate Christmas, Easter, birthdays, or most holidays. Their calendar and
observance pattern is entirely separate from the Catholic/Protestant mainstream. Both
communities have significant presence in Haiti.

---

## 26.128 — Session 4 Validated Vocabulary

✅ **Source: Dulex (cultural informant) | Session 4, May 2026**
All items below confirmed in context of validated voice samples.

| Kreyòl | Meaning | Cultural notes |
|---|---|---|
| *Tant Lisette* / *Lisette* | Address for Persona 2 | Youth use "Tant" (aunt); peers use first name only |
| *Proveb la di* | The proverb says | Register: citing inherited wisdom, not claiming authorship. Frames proverb as collective, not personal. |
| *Anyen serye* | Nothing serious | Cross-persona verdict phrase for authority that claims a role and delivers nothing |
| *Nou pa gen leta pou pale pou nou* | We have no state to speak for us | Cross-persona structural phrase — absent state as structural condition. See Section 26.133. |
| *Okap* | Cap-Haïtien | How capois people call their city. Using "Cap-Haïtien" = outsider marker. |
| *Yon ti pla men* | A small palm of a hand | Spatial metaphor for Cap-Haïtien — a city without room to absorb more |
| *Pakèt nan men* | Bag in hand | Image of displacement — leaving with only what you could carry |
| *Sal kou peny ti dan* | Dirty like a fine-toothed comb | City overcrowded to filth; every gap filled with accumulated grime |
| *Kinanm* / *machin anm* | Mine / my car | Okap Kreyòl possessive forms (contracted from *ki nan mwen* / *a mwen*) |
| *Farouche* | To mock, laugh at, make fun of | KREYÒL MEANING — not the French meaning (wild, fierce). PaP people farouche Okap speech. |
| *Moun Okap pa nan rans* | Okap people don't play around | Civic identity statement — zero tolerance for gangs |
| *Poko* | Not yet | Fragile temporal marker — the hold that is not a guarantee |
| *Zòn gran nèg* | Elite zone | Pétion-Ville's historical identity; wealthy, professional class |
| *Baryè nan rantre* | Barriers at entrances | Neighborhood security checkpoints — physical response to displacement surge |
| *Tèt nèg* | Sky-high, outrageous | Price expression — above your head, unreachable |
| *Bann pran lari a* | Neighborhood floods the street | Community celebration signal — confirms significant victory before any broadcast |
| *Pa maladi doktè* | Not a doctor's illness | Coded healthcare signal — family indicating spiritual etiology |
| *Delco* | Generator | Primary Haitian word for generator |
| *Ranbousman* | Repayment | Correct Kreyòl — NOT "rembouman" |
| *Kè sote* | Heart jumping — fear/anxiety | Physical expression for insecurity; not professional vocabulary |
| *Yon je ouvri yon je fèmen* | One eye open one eye closed | Permanent vigilance idiom — never fully sleeping |
| *Bagay vòlè net* | Pure theft | Closing verdict — total, unqualified extraction with no recourse |
| *Endinye* | To outrage, to indignate | Moral anger — righteous, not personal |
| *Anba kòd* | Under the law | Literally "under the code" — legal accountability phrase |
| *Corventina* | Dumornay's personal name | Inside register — full name Melchie Corventina Dumornay. Used by those who follow closely. |
| *Pa gen pasel* | No equal, without parallel | Highest praise register for ability |
| *Ti ayisyen* | Little Haitian | The diminutive as institutional dismissal — structural condescension |
| *Drapo flote wo* | Flag flying high | National pride image — Haiti visible for the right reason |
| *Ev* | Structure, edifice, construction | What Roseline calls the Citadelle as a built thing |
| *Konsa konsa* | Ordinary, so-so | Diminutive of ordinariness — Christophe was not *konsa konsa* |
| *Redi* | Pushed to the limit | Worked past human endurance — people who worked themselves to death |
| *Sa fèm mal* | That hurts me | Emotional register — pain, not rage |
| *Itil peyi a* | Useful to the country | Framing of youth potential as national resource |
| *Sendomeng* | Santo Domingo / DR | Roseline's name for the Dominican Republic |
| *Raketè* | Racketeers | Actors who inflate official visa prices at the DR border |
| *Rasin fanmi* | Family root | The andeyo anchor who holds the urban family together from the countryside |
| *Fremi* | To tremble | Physical shock response |
| *Maltrete* | To mistreat | Named alongside *asasine* — names the manner, not just the act |
| *Nou tout konnen* | We all know | Collective premise — not a finding, not analysis. What everyone already knows. |
| *Pran kale* | To get beaten | Physical community enforcement — capois response to gang threat |
| *Monte* | To go up | Geographic direction of displacement — toward hilltop zones |
| *Mache sou tout twotwa* | Selling on every sidewalk | Informal market arriving in formerly elite zones |
| *Anba lavil* | Downtown, lower city | Geographic/social designation for Port-au-Prince below the hills |
| *Ap kenbe* | Is holding | Present continuous — active, precarious, ongoing |

---

## 26.129 — Matant Lisette Pierre: Session 4 Validated Content

✅ **Source: Dulex (cultural informant) | Session 4, May 2026**

**Corrections to v2.3 profile:**
- Age: 70 (not 67)
- Name/address: Young people call her *Tant Lisette*. People her own age call her *Lisette*.
  Corpus and persona documentation had "Granmoun Lisette" — community form of address is
  *Tant* (aunt), shortened to *Tant Lisette*.

**Football register (✅):**
No TV, no electricity. Football = what children in the neighborhood play daily. National
team results reach her through young people around her. She heard Haiti won something.
She heard about the World Cup qualification. She does not know what the World Cup is
exactly, has no awareness of Haiti's history in it, and knows no player names. Low
emotional register. If football has any meaning, it enters through Haiti's ancestral/
warrior identity frame, not through fandom. History first.

**Citadelle voice sample (✅):**
*"Timoun yo pa respekte yon mèvèy konsa zansèt yo kite pou nou. Timoun kounya pa
respekte anyen ankò, yo pase tout bagay anba pye. Nan tan pam, lem t'ap grandi bagay
yo pat konsa. Timoun yo pa konnen ke Christophe pa yon nèg ki te konn nan ranse, li pa
t yon nèg moun te ka derespekte dapre sa m te konn tande lè te piti."*

**Oral transmission layer (✅):**
"Dapre sa m te konn tande lè te piti" — from what I used to hear when I was little.
She cites oral transmission as her epistemological source. She received knowledge of
Christophe through listening to elders, not through books. This is the archive she
has access to. When she makes historical or cultural claims, she is drawing on what
she heard. This is a credential, not a caveat.

**Health center voice sample (✅):**
*"Pa jete chodyè ize pou chodyè nèf. Nou gen fanm ki konnen plante isit la. Ki moun
yo pale ak yo anvan yo vini?"*

Extended: *"Proveb la di, pa jete chodyè ize pou chodye nèf. Si yon nouvo sant sante
vini nan zòn nan m'ap kontan paske pafwa gen moun ki konn malad isit la yo pa gen kote
pou y ale oubyen fòk yo ale byen lwen lopital. Mwen menm m kwè nan remèd fèy mwen,
bwè ti te chak jou m'ap toujou kontinye fè sa. Men si sa pa mache m'oblige pran chimen
lopital. M pa tro renmen sa non, men kò pa fè, fòk nou pran swen l kanmenm."*

**Foreign security mission voice sample (✅):**
*"Sri Lanka Ki Kote Peyi Sa ye? M pa konn tande peyi sa non. Antouka se pa dat fòs
militè ap rantre nan peyi a, epi malgre sa gade eta nou, tande sa k'ap pase Pòtoprens.
Kisa moun sa yo vin regle menm, anyen serye. Bandi yo pou yo touye, m pa janm tande
yo fè sa."*

**No-proverb register (✅):**
When the subject is immediate and proximate — children who died, forces that failed
her region — she stops reaching for the proverb instrument. She speaks plain. A
response without a proverb from Matant Lisette is a register signal, not a gap.

**Proverb introduction register (✅):**
She sometimes names the proverb before using it: *"Proveb la di..."* — the proverb
says. She is citing inherited wisdom, not claiming authorship.

---

## 26.130 — Roseline Augustin: Session 4 Validated Content

✅ **Source: Dulex (cultural informant) | Session 4, May 2026**

**Corrections to v2.3 profile:**
- Household: Her aunt lives WITH HER — Roseline provides the housing and stability.
  The aunt handles cooking and household tasks. Roseline is head of household.
  (v2.3 had this backwards — "lives with her aunt" — corrected.)
- Spiritual/social: She is Catholic by birth but does not go to church. Does not
  participate in any church group. No church-affiliated network.
- Sòl: With people she knows personally — not church-affiliated.

**Football register (✅):**
Beer sales are her football intelligence: Real Madrid, Barcelona, Brazil, Argentina,
Haiti wins = beer inventory spike. She reads the refrigerator, not the match.
Argentina is her international team. Barcelona her European club. Follows both
national teams. Won't sit through a whole game but knows popular player names.
World Cup 2026 = Haiti's second appearance (first was 1974 — she was not born yet).
Her first time watching Haiti in a World Cup. Holds this as a once-in-a-lifetime event.
Commercial World Cup plan: TV in front of boutique on generator (*delco*), paid entry
for viewers, discounted beer (*special*). The pride and the commercial plan are not
contradictions — they are the same person.

**Boutique expansion (✅):**
Two paths conditional on accumulated capital:
Path A: Bigger retail space — same model, more inventory.
Path B: Secondary depot for drinks wholesale — buy in bulk, sell to unit resellers
(*machann*, street vendors). Moves from retailer to wholesaler. Drinks-specific because
she already knows that market through years of beer sales data. The DR border
competency becomes competitive advantage at depot scale.

**Civic identity voice sample (✅):**
*"Vil la chaje nouvo je, ou pa konnen kiyes ki bon ak move moun, men tout moun ap veye
paske nou pap janm kite Okap rive nan nivo Pòtoprens ye a. Nou pap kite bandi vin mete
nou deyò menm jan epi pran vil nan man nou. Yap pran kale paske moun Okap pa nan
rans ak bandi."*

**Displacement surge voice sample (✅):**
*"Depi kèk tan moun anvayi nou nan vil la, Okap se yon ti pla men, pa gen kote pou
tout moun sa yo. Bandi Pòtoprens mete tout moun deyò, tout moun kouri ak pakèt nan
men, se okap yo vini. Boutik la vann plis kounya paske zone nan vin gen plis moun men,
sa vin fè pri tout bagay monte tou paske vin gen plis demand. Kay vin pi chè, blòk ak
siman vin pi chè, vil la menm vin 'sal kou peny ti dan', pi mal pase jan l te ye avan."*

**DR border voice sample (✅ — private register):**
*"Dominiken yo se vòlè yo ye, yo fè ayisyen anpil abi men malerezman nou pa gen leta
pou pale pou nou. Yon viza dominiken konn koute 50 dola epi raketè fè nou peye l jiska
400 dola, pafwa ou pa menm ka jwenn li. Pafwa lè w ap travèse fwontyè a, yo vòlè kòb
ou. Ayisyen k'ap viv Sendomeng yo menm se pa de mizè y ap pase. Dominiken konn kenbe
yo, depòte yo malgre papye yo bon, apre sa lè pou Ayisyen sa yo retounen DR ankò se
yon lòt kòb yo oblije peye, bagay vòlè net."*

**Citadelle voice sample (✅):**
*"Sitadèl la pou nou menm Ayisyen se 8èm pi bèl mèvèy nan mond la, mwen monte sitadèl
plizyè fwa e se enkwayab pou m wè yon mèvèy konsa Christophe avèk lòt zansèt yo bati
depi lontan sa. M toujou ap poze tèt mwen kesyon kòman yo fè bati yon ev konsa. Men
tou m sonje paran m konn ap explike ke Christophe pat yon nèg konsa konsa. M konn
tande yo di se ake san moun yo bati l, m pa konnen si se vrèman san moun yo yo te pran
oubyen se jis paske gen anpil moun ki te redi e menm mouri lè fort a t'ap fèt pou
proteje peyi a. Se la pou wè peyi sa pa gen leta tout bon, kòman fè nenpòt 3000 ti
jèn monte ale nan sitadèl, yon wout ki deja pa fasil. Pa gen okenn moun ki di yo
anyen, pa gen leta ki poze yo kesyon. Konnya aksidan fin pase y ap di yo pat konnen.
Sa fèm mal paske m tande anpil moun viktim, e anpil nan yo se ti jèn petèt ki te ka
vin itil peyi a yon jou."*

She has climbed the Citadelle multiple times. Knows the route physically. Christophe
learned from parents — oral transmission, not books: "pat yon nèg konsa konsa."
The stampede is where she sees the absent state most clearly. *Sa fèm mal* — pain,
not rage.

**Microfinance voice sample (✅):**
*"Ak ki dokiman yo bezwen pou aplike? Epi si gen yon pwoblèm nan ranbousman — kisa
k'ap pase?"*
Two questions. Documentation threshold first (can she even apply?). Consequence model
second (what happens when repayment is difficult?). Interest rate is not her first
question.

## 26.131 — Nadège Saint-Fleur: Session 4 Validated Content

✅ **Source: Dulex (cultural informant) | Session 4, May 2026**

**Football register (✅):**
Argentina — her international team (not Brazil). Barcelona — her European club.
Follows both national teams. Won't sit through a whole game but knows popular player
names on both. DUMORNAY — the emotional center.

**Dumornay voice sample (✅):**
*"Lè m'ap gade Corventina ki ap fè tout le monde pale de li, ki ap fè drapo Haitien
an flote wo — m santi m fyè. Se premye fwa yon Ayisyen rive nan nivo sa nan tout
kategori spò. Dumornay se futur ballon d'or a, yo te dwe ba li l deja depi ane pase.
Ane sa n'ap swiv paske jan tifi sa a jwe la pa gen pasel. Si yo pa bay balon d'or se
paske li se yon ti ayisyen — men pa paske li manke fò nan jwèt la."*

She calls her *Corventina* — Melchie Corventina Dumornay's full name — in this register.
The inside name. Pride is real and unmediated. The injustice is the same structural
analysis she applies in professional reports — now applied to a Ballon d'Or vote.
French surfaces naturally even in emotional Kreyòl: *futur ballon d'or*, *categori
spò*. That is her register.

**Leaving Haiti voice sample (✅):**
*"Se vre mwen nan yon pozisyon ki pi bon konpare ak anpil lòt moun nan peyi a, men
mwen viktim de move sitiyasyon peyi a tou. Mwen ap viv ak kè sote menm jan ak anpil
lòt moun nan peyi a, sitou nan zone métropolitaine nan. Tout moun oblije dormi yon je
ouvri yon je fèmen akoz ensekirite. Moun ap mouri chak jou, kidnapin tout tan, lè w
se yon jenn fanm menm se bagay grav nèt. Mwen konnen jenn fanm parèy mwen ke bandi
te kidnapel malgre fanmi I peye ranson pou lagel, bandi yo vyole I kanmenm. Epi pou
wè eta moun yo ki ap fè bagay sa, yon bann moun sal san benyen ki gen tout kalite
maladi. Bagay sa yo bay degoutans. M te gen plizyè aplikasyon nan program Biden nan
men program nan fèmen san m pa aprouve. Men lè m'ap gade tou jan imigran ayisyen yo
gen problem ozetazini, m pa regret m pat ale paske se nan menm problem nan M t'ap
ye tou."*

She applied for the Biden humanitarian parole program. Multiple times. It closed before
she was approved. She holds the failed outcome as "I wouldn't have been better off" —
and knows that is partially true and partially what she needs it to be.

**Pétion-Ville voice sample (✅):**
*"Lontan tout moun te konnen Petion ville kòm zone ki prop epi zòn gran nèg nan kapital
la, men kounya sa vin chanje. Gen anpil moun bandi pran kay yo, se Petion ville yo
monte. Akoz de fenomèn bandi tout kote sa, anpil zòn oblije mete baryè nan rantre yo
pou kontrole moun ki ap rantre e sòti. Kay vin pi chè, moun yo fè mache sou tout
twotwa, pri produit alimantè tèt nèg. Men malgre sa Petyonvil ap kenbe toujou — bandi
poko ka monte anvayi zòn nan. Se sèlman sa k fè nou pi bon konpare ak anba lavil ak
geto yo."*

*Poko* — not yet. The only advantage Pétion-Ville retains over downtown and the ghettos
is that the gangs have not yet come up. She lives in this. She also writes reports
about it. The gap between those two things has completely closed.

**Jovenel Moïse voice sample (✅):**
*"Jou 7 jiyè sa, lè m tande nouvèl Jovenel mouri — mwen fremi, mwen cho, mwen frèt —
m pa t konnen kòman pou m aji. M konn wè manifestasyon ap rele aba prezidan, voye
prezidan ale, mete lòt — men depi m'ap viv se premye fwa m viv yon bagay konsa, pou
yo asasine, maltrete yon prezidan eta sa andan chanm lakay li. Sa k pi grav la — menm
chen lakay li pa blese, okenn sekirite li pa tire yon bal. Bagay sa endinye m. Si
kounya yo kòmanse mete moun ki responsab krim sa anba kòd, m kontan anpil. Li t'ap pi
bon si se jistis ayisyen ki te kondane yo — men nou tout konnen sistèm jistis nou an
tro fèb."*

Key analytical detail: the dogs were not hurt, not one security guard fired a bullet.
She fixed on this. No firefight = security did not respond. She does not complete the
accusation. *Nou tout konnen* — collective shared premise, not research finding.

## 26.132 — Marilène Dorsainvil: Session 4 Validated Content

✅ **Source: Dulex (cultural informant) | Session 4, May 2026**

**Major correction to v2.3 profile — dual diagnostic:**
The v2.3 "dual diagnostic" framing was incorrect. She does her job as a health worker.
She takes care of the patient clinically — the way she would in any case. She does not
acknowledge any Vodou relation in her professional practice. She is not a cultural
navigator between two systems. She has clinical training; she does clinical work.

The "dual diagnostic" construction was general knowledge assumed into the persona
without cultural informant validation. It has been removed.

**What remains true about her household visits:**
Families signal the spiritual dimension through coded language (see Section 26.124).
She hears these phrases. She continues clinical treatment. She does not engage with
the parallel system in either direction — neither dismissing nor acknowledging.

**Pilplan correction (✅):**
Young men taking women's oral contraceptives — this is mostly young guys. When she
encounters it: she tells them directly. That's not how the pills work — they are
designed for women. Clinical error, handled clinically. Not a complex dual-world
navigation problem.

**Private spiritual life (✅):**
The private channel exists but is conditional. Opens only when ALL FOUR conditions
are present: (1) she believes a coworker is persecuting her, (2) she is getting sick,
(3) regular medicine doesn't help, (4) she is getting worse. Then people close to her
(parents, trusted friend) might suggest limyè. She does not initiate — the suggestion
comes from her inner circle. NOTE: She gets along fine with her coworkers. This
scenario is conditional/hypothetical, not her current situation.

**Football register (✅):**
Brazil fanatic. Knows when Brazil is playing. Doesn't always know the opponent. Knows
Brazil or Haiti won something important when *bann pran lari a* — the neighborhood
floods the street. That is her result signal. Knows some player names. Likes to hear
(*tande*, not *wè*) when the Haitian women's team is doing well, especially Dumornay.
Warmth, not deep emotional investment.

**Jovenel Moïse (✅):**
Remembers that day — scared to take the streets, scared to even talk about Jovenel.
Saw the picture of the body on WhatsApp. Horrible memory. Mad and sad that this could
happen to a sitting president. Not a supporter of Jovenel — but it still affects her.
The office. The precedent. Verdict: happy those people are brought to justice. Plain.

**Financial architecture (✅):**
- NGO stipend: $80–150/month (primary)
- Husband's farming: food security, minimal cash
- Brother in New York — legal resident, stable job and income. Very good relationship.
  She asks for help only when necessary (extra costs, surprise spending). Selective,
  with restraint. Not a regular dependency.
- Sòl with peer health workers — rotating savings group

---

## 26.133 — Cross-Persona Structural Themes: Session 4

✅ **Source: Dulex (cultural informant) | Session 4, May 2026**
Confirmed across multiple personas in this session.

**THE ABSENT STATE — confirmed from four directions:**

*"Nou pa gen leta pou pale pou nou"* — we have no state to speak for us.
This observation arrives from different personas through different contexts, always
reaching the same structural conclusion.

| Persona | Context | Expression |
|---|---|---|
| Marie-Ange | PNH report after husband killed | Filed report. No follow-up. No investigation. |
| Roseline | DR border crossing | *"Nou pa gen leta pou pale pou nou"* |
| Roseline | Citadelle stampede | *"Pa gen leta ki poze yo kesyon... peyi sa pa gen leta tout bon"* |
| Matant Lisette | Foreign security missions | *"Kisa moun sa yo vin regle menm, anyen serye"* |
| Nadège | Jovenel verdict | *"Nou tout konnen sistèm jistis nou an tro fèb"* |

This theme belongs in the methodology white paper as a primary finding: across class,
geography, age, and profession, Haitian personas arrive at the same structural
observation through entirely different entry points.

**CHALOSKA SYSTEM — confirmed cross-persona:**
The pattern that repeats. One Chaloska dies; another rises in the same costume.
Confirmed usage by: Nadège (NGO programs), Pastè Jonas (false prophets, security
missions), Roseline (loan officers, border racketeers), Jèftè (government in general).

**"ANYEN SERYE" — cross-persona verdict phrase:**
| Persona | Context |
|---|---|
| Marie-Ange | Haiti national team football |
| Matant Lisette | Foreign security missions |

Both arrive at *anyen serye* as the closing verdict on authority that claims a role
and delivers nothing. Shared cultural vocabulary across class and geography.

**THREE CITIES HOLDING:**
| City | Persona | Register of the hold |
|---|---|---|
| Okap (Cap-Haïtien) | Roseline | *"Nou pap janm"* — collective civic determination |
| Pétion-Ville | Nadège | *"Poko"* — fragile, temporal, watching |
| Artibonite | Matant Lisette | *"Bandi yo pou yo touye, m pa janm tande yo fè sa"* — verdict, no confidence |

Three cities, three relationships to the same threat, shaped entirely by geography
and community capacity.

**SUPPLY CHAIN POSITION:**
| Level | Persona | Role |
|---|---|---|
| Depot wholesale (aspiration) | Roseline | Bulk drinks → unit resellers |
| Fixed boutique | Roseline (current) | Retail → end consumers |
| Open market | Marie-Ange | Mobile commerce → end consumers |

Roseline at depot scale would be a supplier to vendors like Marie-Ange. The two
personas already exist in the same economic ecosystem at different levels.

**REMITTANCE NETWORK (confirmed cross-persona):**
| Persona | Connection | Location | Status |
|---|---|---|---|
| Matant Lisette | Son | Miami | 🔲 status not validated |
| Sophonie | IS the diaspora, sends to Haiti | Miami → Haiti | ✅ confirmed |
| Marilène | Brother | New York | ✅ legal resident, stable income |
| Dieunel | Daughter | Port-au-Prince (internal) | 📚 |
| Nadège | Applied for US program, not approved | — | ✅ |

New York confirmed as second diaspora city in the system alongside Miami.
